{"fully-automated-luxury-communism": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">It starts with a burger.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In 2008 a Dutch professor named Mark Post presented the proof of concept for what he called \"cultured meat.\" Five years later, in a London TV studio, Mr. Post and his colleagues ate a burger they had grown from animal cells in a laboratory. Secretly funded by Sergey Brin, a co-founder of Google, the journey from petri dish to plate had cost $325,000 \u2014 making theirs the most expensive meal in history. Fortunately, the results were promising: Hanni R\\xfctzler, a nutrition scientist, concluded that the patty was \"<a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.newscientist.com/article/dn23996-whats-the-beef-cultured-meat-remains-a-distant-dream/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">close to meat but not as juicy</a>.\" The next question was whether this breakthrough could be made cheaper. Much cheaper.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The first \"cultured <!-- -->beef<!-- -->\" burgers are likely to enter the market next year, at approximately $50 each. But that won't last long. Within a decade they will probably be more affordable than even the cheapest barbecue staples of today \u2014 all for a product that uses fewer resources, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://www.ox.ac.uk/news/2011-06-21-lab-grown-meat-would-cut-emissions-and-save-energy\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">produces negligible greenhouse gases</a> and, remarkably, requires no animals to die.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">It's not just barbecues and burgers. Last year Just, a leader in cellular agriculture, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.foodnavigator-usa.com/Article/2018/12/11/JUST-strikes-deal-in-Japan-to-bring-cell-cultured-Wagyu-beef-to-market\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">cut a deal</a> to start producing one of the world's tastiest steaks, Wagyu. A company called Endless West, which also makes grapeless wine, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://endlesswest.com/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">has started to produce Glyph</a>, the world's first \"molecular whiskey.\" Luxury could be coming to all.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The case of cultured food and drink, far from a curiosity, is a template for a better, freer and more affluent world, a world where we provide for the needs of everyone \u2014 in style.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But how do we get there?</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">To say the present era is one of crisis borders on clich\\xe9. It differs from the dystopias of George Orwell or Aldous Huxley, or hell in the paintings of Hieronymus Bosch. It is unlike Europe during the Black Death or Central Asia as it faced the galloping Golden Horde. And yet it is true: Ours is an age of crisis. We inhabit a world of low growth, low productivity and low wages, of climate breakdown and the collapse of democratic politics. A world where billions, mostly in the global south, live in poverty. A world defined by inequality.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But the most pressing crisis of all, arguably, is an absence of collective imagination. It is as if humanity has been afflicted by a psychological complex, in which we believe the present world is stronger than our capacity to remake it \u2014 as if it were not our ancestors who created what stands before us now. As if the very essence of humanity, if there is such a thing, is not to constantly build new worlds.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">If we can move beyond such a failure, we will be able to see something wonderful. The plummeting cost of information and advances in technology are providing the ground for a collective future of freedom and luxury for all. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Automation, robotics and machine learning will, as many august bodies, from the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/3cea8516-8963-11e5-90de-f44762bf9896\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Bank of England</a> to the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.huffingtonpost.co.uk/entry/white-house-robot-workers_n_56cdd89ce4b0928f5a6de955\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">White House</a>, have predicted, substantially shrink the work force, creating widespread technological unemployment. But that's only a problem if you think work \u2014 as a cashier, driver or construction worker \u2014 is something to be cherished. For many, work is drudgery. And automation could set us free from it.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Gene editing and sequencing could revolutionize medical practice, moving it from reactive to predictive. Hereditary diseases could be eliminated, including Huntington's disease, cystic fibrosis and sickle cell anemia, and cancer cured before it reaches Stage 1. Those technologies could allow us to keep pace with the health challenges presented by societal aging \u2014 by 2020 there will be <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.who.int/news-room/fact-sheets/detail/ageing-and-health\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">more people over the age of 60</a> than under the age of 5 \u2014 and even to surpass them.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">What's more, renewable energy, which has been experiencing steep annual falls in cost for half a century, could meet global energy needs and make possible the vital shift away from fossil fuels. More speculatively, asteroid mining \u2014 whose technical barriers are presently being surmounted \u2014 could provide us with not only more energy than we can ever imagine but also more iron, gold, platinum and nickel. Resource scarcity would be a thing of the past.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The consequences are far-reaching and potentially transformative. For the crises that confront our world today \u2014 technological unemployment, global poverty, societal aging, climate change, resource scarcity \u2014 we can already glimpse the remedy.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But there's a catch. It's called capitalism. It has created the newly emerging abundance, but it is unable to <!-- -->share round<!-- --> the fruits of technological development. A system where things are produced only for profit, capitalism seeks to ration resources to ensure returns. Just like today's, companies of the future will form monopolies and seek rents. The result will be imposed scarcity \u2014 where there's not enough food, health care or energy to go around.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">So we have to go beyond capitalism. Many will find this suggestion unwholesome. To them, the claim that capitalism will or should end is like saying a triangle doesn't have three sides or that the law of gravity no longer applies while an apple falls from a tree. But for a better world, where everyone has the means to a good life on a habitable planet, it is an imperative.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">We can see the contours of something new, a society as distinct from our own as that of the 20th century from feudalism, or urban civilization from the life of the hunter-gatherer. It builds on technologies whose development has been accelerating for decades and that only now are set to undermine the key features of what we had previously taken for granted as the natural order of things.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">To grasp it, however, will require a new politics. One where technological change serves people, not profit. Where the pursuit of tangible policies \u2014 rapid decarbonization, full automation and socialized care \u2014 are preferred to present fantasies. This politics, which is utopian in horizon and everyday in application, has a name: Fully Automated Luxury Communism.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Sounds good, doesn't it?</p><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\">Aaron Bastani (<a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://twitter.com/AaronBastani\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">@AaronBastani</a>) is a co-founder of Novara Media and the author of the forthcoming \"Fully Automated Luxury Communism: A Manifesto,\" from which this essay is adapted. </p><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">The Times is committed to publishing </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/31/opinion/letters/letters-to-editor-new-york-times-women.html\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">a diversity of letters</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\"> to the editor. We Need Fully Automated Luxury Communism. - The New York Times</title>"}, "hong-kong-protests": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">If we are to believe <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/26/world/asia/hong-kong-election-carrie-lam-chief-executive.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">Carrie Lam</a>, the chief executive of the Hong Kong government, the hundreds of thousands of people who marched through the city's sweltering streets on Sunday just didn't get it. They may have thought they were <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/09/world/asia/hong-kong-extradition-protest.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">protesting a proposal</a> to allow extradition of criminal suspects to mainland China, but, in Ms. Lam's view, they failed to understand that the measure would ensure that the city did not become a haven for fugitives and that existing legal protections and human rights would remain in force.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">And if we are to believe the press in mainland China, that vast throng was really \"some Hong Kong residents\" who had been \"hoodwinked by the opposition camp and their foreign allies\" into opposing the legislation, to cite <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://www.chinadaily.com.cn/a/201906/09/WS5cfd0916a3101765772301f8.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">the version in China Daily</a>, an organ of the Chinese Communist Party.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">No, Ms. Lam and editors of China Daily, the people of Hong Kong were not \"hoodwinked,\" nor did they misunderstand this legislation.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">They understand very clearly that the measure making its way through the local legislature, where pro-Beijing deputies hold sway, has nothing to do with bringing murderers to justice, and everything to do with breaking down the firewall between Hong Kong's rule of law and mainland China's thoroughly politicized judicial system. They understand that the legislation represents a further <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/10/world/asia/hong-kong-china-protests-explained.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">encroachment by Beijing into the </a><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/10/world/asia/hong-kong-china-protests-explained.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">\"high degree of autonomy\"</a><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/10/world/asia/hong-kong-china-protests-explained.html?module=inline\" title=\"\"> Hong Kong was promised</a> when Britain returned the territory to <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/1997/07/01/world/china-resumes-control-of-hong-kong-concluding-156-years-of-british-rule.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">Chinese sovereignty in 1997</a>.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Ms. Lam, at least, did not publicly question the motives of the protesters, who came out in <!-- -->the biggest numbers<!-- --> since at least the 1997 handover. <!-- -->\"<!-- -->I believe most of the protesters yesterday loved Hong Kong and came out for the sake of the next generation<!-- -->,\" she said.<!-- --> In pledging to protect human rights, she at least acknowledged the core concern of the residents of every age and calling who so jam-packed the downtown streets that other people couldn't get out of subway stations.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Beijing, by contrast, showed its true colors by playing down the protests and spreading the shopworn canard that they were the work of \"<!-- -->foreign forces<!-- -->.\" </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"We firmly oppose any outside interference in the legislative affairs\" <!-- -->of the region,<!-- --> intoned the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.straitstimes.com/asia/east-asia/foreign-forces-seeking-to-create-havoc-in-hong-kong-chinese-paper-says\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Foreign Ministry spokesman, Geng Shuang</a>, perhaps oblivious to the irony that the only interference was by his government.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/10/world/asia/hong-kong-carrie-lam-extradition.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">Ms. Lam has not backed down</a> on the extradition bill, and neither she nor the city legislature is <!-- -->likely<!-- --> to buck Beijing.<!-- --> Under Hong Kong's limited democracy, the chief executive is approved by Beijing and only half the seats in the legislature are filled by popular vote, though Ms. Lam insisted on Monday that the extradition bill was not imported from the mainland.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The residents of Hong Kong demonstrated once again that they will not easily surrender the civil liberties they learned to regard as their self-evident due under British rule. Five years ago, protesters of the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2014/10/01/world/asia/hong-kong-protest-photos.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">Umbrella Movement</a> occupied central city streets for 79 days to demand more transparent elections. And in 2003, an effort to enact a package of <!-- -->law<!-- -->s prohibiting sedition, subversion and treason against the Chinese government was shelved after half a million residents poured into the streets in protest.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Hong Kong's freedoms are a standing irritant to the Communist authorities in Beijing, who have not ceased chipping away at them. One example is a draft law to criminalize <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/10/16/world/asia/china-yang-kaili-anthem.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">disrespect for the Chinese national anthem</a>; another is the disappearance of people from Hong Kong into mainland custody.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/07/world/asia/hong-kong-china-extradition-protest.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">The extradition measure </a>was initially presented as needed to send a Hong Kong man to Taiwan, where he allegedly killed his girlfriend. But to the democracy-minded people of Hong Kong, this was only cover for a portion of the bill that would also allow extradition to mainland China, which would enable Chinese authorities to pry political foes from Hong Kong by leveling false accusations and demanding their extradition. That, in effect, would extend China's reach into Hong Kong and strip its residents of the protection of the law.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Sunday's protesters vowed to be back in the streets when the bill next comes before the legislature. If Ms. Lam really believes they are acting out of concern for \"the next generation,\" she would do well to heed them and shelve this cynical assault on Hong Kong's rule of law.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-g92qtk epkadsg3\"><div class=\"css-1owp1gq epkadsg0\">Related</div><div class=\"css-ckpga5 epkadsg1\">More Times coverage of the Hong Kong protests.</div><div class=\"css-15g2oxy epkadsg2\"><div class=\"css-2b3w4o e16ij5yr6\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/10/opinion/hong-kong-extradition-protest-china.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedLinks&amp;pgtype=Article\"><div class=\"css-i9gxme e16ij5yr4\"><div class=\"css-14b9hti e16ij5yr5\">Opinion | Yi-Zheng Lian</div><div class=\"css-1j8dw05 e16ij5yr2\">Hong Kong's Government May Cave In to China. The New York Times</title>"}, "budapest-danube-crash": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">BUDAPEST \u2014 Long before Hungary's <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/30/world/europe/budapest-boat-accident.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">worst boating accident</a> in at least six decades, Hungarian officials had been warned that traffic on the Danube had soared to dangerous levels around Budapest, but the government did not curb the number of vessels plying the river.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">On the night of May 29, in a driving rain, an international cruise ship, the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.vikingrivercruises.co.uk/ships/longships/viking-sigyn.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Viking Sigyn</a> struck and sank a smaller sightseeing boat, the Mermaid, killing 28 people. The cause is still under investigation, but the accident has raised concerns that at the municipal and national levels, where tourism has become a major source of revenue, political calculations and the drive for profit outweighed safety concerns.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Either the national government or the city, both controlled by Prime Minister Viktor Orban's Fidesz party, could have acted to limit the number of ships and boats operating in Budapest; the national tourism agency grants permits to sightseeing vessels, while the city controls access to the docks. Both declined to comment.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"City officials were warned about the dangers of too much traffic,\" said Gabor Demszky, the mayor of Budapest from 1990 to 2010. \"But they failed to act. It is a very profitable business.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">On Tuesday, a floating crane slowly lifted the Mermaid to the surface, and divers recovered four bodies from the wreck. The vessel carried 33 tourists from South Korea and two crew members; only seven of those aboard survived, and several of the victims have still not been found.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The 64-year-old Ukrainian captain of the Viking Sigyn, identified only as Yuriy C., has been arrested on suspicion of negligence. Viking Cruises confirmed reports that he was part of the crew of another ship, the Viking Idun, that was involved in a collision in the Netherlands in April, raising questions about how he had been allowed to take the helm of one of the newest and largest vessels in the company's fleet.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube2/merlin_156277461_edd752e8-791d-42b3-a678-1fc8fc182280-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><img alt=\"\" class=\"css-1m50asq\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube2/merlin_156277461_edd752e8-791d-42b3-a678-1fc8fc182280-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" itemprop=\"url\" sizes=\"((min-width: 600px) and (max-width: 1004px)) 84vw, (min-width: 1005px) 80vw, 100vw\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube2/merlin_156277461_edd752e8-791d-42b3-a678-1fc8fc182280-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" srcset=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube2/merlin_156277461_edd752e8-791d-42b3-a678-1fc8fc182280-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube2/merlin_156277461_edd752e8-791d-42b3-a678-1fc8fc182280-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube2/merlin_156277461_edd752e8-791d-42b3-a678-1fc8fc182280-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w\"/></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Four bodies were recovered from the Mermaid on Tuesday.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Marton Monus/EPA, via Shutterstock</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But beyond the role of human error, people have long pointed to the risks of heavy river traffic through Budapest \u2014 especially at night, when tourist vessels offer views of the city at its most spectacular. City officials have been warned, in at least two reports, that the number of vessels navigating this stretch of the Danube and the lack of communication between international and local ships could pose a danger.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">A 2013 <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://budapest.hu/Documents/V%C3%A1ros%C3%A9p%C3%ADt%C3%A9si%20F%C5%91oszt%C3%A1ly/_Budapest%20Duna-menti%20ter%C3%BCeteinek%20fejleszt%C3%A9si%20tanulm%C3%A1nyterve%201.%20k%C3%B6tet.pdf\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">development study</a> commissioned by the city warned that the increase in hotel boats \"has led to numerous points of tension,\" including overcrowding on the waterway. This year, a <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://budapest.hu/Documents/20190411_Bp_Mobilit%C3%A1si_Terv_2030_egyeztet%C3%A9si%20v%C3%A1ltozat.pdf\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">transportation development study</a> prepared by the Budapest Transportation Authority found that more \"cooperation was needed between professional and tourism-related vessels on the Budapest\" stretch of the Danube.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The newest cruise ships, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.vikingrivercruises.co.uk/ships/longships/index.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">known as longships</a>, are essentially floating hotels, stretching up to 500 feet long and able to accommodate nearly 1,000 guests.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Hotel ships, like the 442-foot Viking Sigyn, must compete for space with local sightseeing vessels like the Mermaid, an 89-foot, Soviet-era vessel, as well as with industrial transport barges, permanently docked restaurants and other floating structures used for entertainment. Budapest residents say the increased volume is striking, as is the rise in air pollution from the ships.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The Danube stretches some 1,800 miles from Germany to the Black Sea and flows through 10 countries, making it hard to get a complete picture of river traffic and safety.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.inland-navigation-market.org/en/rapports/2018/q2/7-river-cruises/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">a study cofinanced by the European Commission</a> released in April 2018 found that the amount of traffic on the Danube, measured at the German-Austrian border, increased by 89 percent from 2002 to 2017. It also reported that the number of cruise vessels plying the river more than doubled from 2004 to 2017, to 346 ships with 50,616 beds.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Capt. Branislav Vajda, the president of the Association of Professional Carriers of Serbia, said that crowding on the Danube in and around Belgrade, that country's capital, was so severe, \"it is only a matter of time before we have a tragedy of our own to announce.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube3/merlin_155817591_5fe64e66-5b53-4a1a-8f0c-e001b6e294b5-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:264.8666666666667px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">A memorial to the victims of the capsized boat near the Margaret Bridge in Budapest.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Balazs Mohai/EPA, via Shutterstock</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">As King Victor Emmanuel III of Italy found <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/1937/05/20/archives/54-hurt-as-budapest-hails-victor-emmanuel-the-citys-first-royal.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">when he visited Budapest in 1937</a> and his hosts lit up the majestic Chain Bridge for the first time, the city's imperial grandeur is at its most magical at night. And the best vantage point for seeing the sights, from Buda Castle to the monumental Parliament building, is the river.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"The government and the oligarchs around the government officials, are always looking for new resources and, in this business, they found one,\" said Mr. Demszky, the former mayor.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">He said that the current mayor, Istvan Tarlos, an ally of Mr. Orban, was supported by the national government, \"so he is not really free to act.\" Mr. Tarlos declined to respond to a request for an interview.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In the days after the accident, according to people familiar with the tourism industry, scores of boats seemed to disappear as the authorities cracked down on those operating without the proper permits. But many said they believed the moves were only temporary.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Mr. Orban and his Fidesz party have near complete control over the state and have been exerting increasing influence over the private economy, including tourism, one of the most profitable sectors. Mr. Orban's daughter, Rahel Orban, who has a master's degree in hospitality management from the private <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.ehl.edu/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">\\xc9cole H\\xf4teli\\xe8re de Lausanne</a> in Switzerland, is an unpaid adviser to the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://abouthungary.hu/hungarian-tourism-agency/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Hungarian Tourism Agency</a>.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In 2016, Mr. Orban earmarked more than $3 billion in public funds for tourism ventures across Hungary up to 2030, including a $1 billion resort complex near Lake Balaton. Ms. Orban's husband, Istvan Tiborcz, has come under criticism for his stake in the development. <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.reuters.com/investigates/special-report/hungary-orban-balaton/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">A Reuters investigation published in 2018</a> found that Mr. Tiborcz \"stands to collect almost half of any profits from a venture which acquired the resort's biggest hotel.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The Hungarian Tourism Agency, which manages all tourism-related projects, including those funded by the European Union, is overseen by the Prime Minister's Office and co-owns the slips for international ships along the Budapest stretch of the Danube.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube4/merlin_155888937_3849bf0e-be9f-412f-aeb3-20bc649456ab-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">A Korean folk song was sung on June 3 near the scene of the accident in tribute to the victims, many of whom were from South Korea.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Zoltan Balogh/EPA, via Shutterstock</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"The authorities should examine whether business considerations unduly overruled expert opinions that the increased hotel boat traffic on the Danube River in Budapest may cause serious accidents,\" said Miklos Ligeti, legal director for the public information advocacy group <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://transparency.hu/en/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Transparency International</a> in Hungary. \"If this can be established, there is a serious indication of gross negligence which should be prosecuted.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Officials from Viking Cruises declined to answer questions about overcrowding on the river, but industry officials noted that river cruise ships remain among the safest modes of travel, with a record better even than the airline industry.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Zsolt Varga, head of the Hungarian Federation of Passenger Fleet Operators, said he did not believe that the recent tragedy was the result of overcrowding.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Those two boats could have been the only boats on the Danube at that time and this still could have happened,\" he said.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Still, he acknowledged that there was concern about coordination between local boats and the larger cruise ships. That is why, he said, a new rule was instituted last year requiring ships doing a sightseeing loop in Budapest to travel past the Arpad Bridge in the north and Rakoczi Bridge in the south before making turns.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">David Szekeres, a 47-year-old boat captain who trains skippers with his Gabriella Sailing company, said navigating around Budapest presented specific challenges, including jetties unmarked on maps and navigation markers in the wrong places. Within the city, the Danube rises and falls as much as eight meters \u2014 more than in other cities, where dams and levees regulate the flow. When the river is running high and fast, it carries all sorts of debris, and leaves little room for error passing under bridges.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Not all those at the helm are up to the task, Mr. Szekeres said, in part because the licensing process has been weakened.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/world/11danube5/merlin_156134730_11f0cf82-bf34-4e74-a549-cba2317e3fc9-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">The vessel carried 33 tourists from South Korea and two crew members; only seven of those aboard survived. Several of the victims have still not been found.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Balazs Mohai/MTI, via Associated Press</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">For instance, he said that the test for a pilot license for boats under 20 feet changed in 2013, when a former government official took over a company that trained pilots for the written part of the exam.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"You don't have to learn anything about sailing,\" he said. \"You just have to learn the exact answers to pass the test.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">It was near the Margaret Bridge that the accident took place.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">As the Viking ship bore down on the Mermaid from behind, investigators said, there was no radio communication between them. No warning horn was sounded.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The inquiry has been hampered by treacherous currents and poor underwater visibility. The Viking ship left Budapest for Passau, Germany, less than two days after the fatal collision.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Gyorgy Magyar, a Hungarian lawyer representing the family of the Hungarian crewman aboard the Mermaid, said it was wrong for the authorities to allow the Viking to depart from Budapest so soon after the accident.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"That vessel was involved in an accident and it is evidence that shouldn't be released until the professional and all-encompassing investigation has concluded,\" he said. Letting it leave means \"the evidence has been tampered with,\" he added.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Some clues as to the cause of the crash might be revealed now that the Mermaid has been recovered from the riverbed. But whatever investigators find, it will not change what people who know the Danube have long said is the basic problem.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"For me, it is overcrowded,\" Mr. Szekeres said.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"And now, you have these really big cruise ships doing sightseeing tours, and they are just too big,\" he added. \"They should not be doing this. Especially at night.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/11/world/europe/budapest-danube-crash.html", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">Before Fatal Boat Crash in Budapest, Safety Warnings Went Unheeded - The New York Times</title>"}, "youtube-radicalization-algorithms": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In the last month there have been two big profiles, one in this newspaper and one in Washingtonian, of young men who were radicalized into some version of the alt-right and then later abjured far-right politics.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.washingtonian.com/2019/05/05/what-happened-after-my-13-year-old-son-joined-the-alt-right/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Washingtonian profile</a> is a mother's first-person account of watching her 13-year-old son join an extremist internet community and then find his way back out. <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/06/08/technology/youtube-radical.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">The Times profile</a>, by my colleague Kevin Roose, follows a 20-something college dropout who has turned to progressive politics after a sojourn as a <!-- -->\"tradcon.\"<!-- --> Both pieces locate their subjects in a larger sociology, but both are especially concerned with the role of YouTube in accelerating radicalization, and in particular with the way its algorithm, intended to reward videos that prompt intense engagement, is creating a pathway into extremist content by rewarding provocation and letting content purveyors essentially monetize the rabbit hole.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Since I might be described (even in the comment thread below this column, who knows?) as some sort of \"tradcon\" myself, I have some doubts about categorizations that purport to define the moment when respectable conservatism becomes dangerous extremism. Nonetheless I agree with several of the profiles' anti-YouTube premises: Education-by-algorithm is a bad idea; Silicon Valley has monetized amoral slippery slopes in all kinds of arenas (with pedophilia being the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/03/world/americas/youtube-pedophiles.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">latest grim example</a>); and the stew of racism and conspiracy theory at the far-right edges of social media is an example of where one such slope can lead.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">That said, the profiles are rich enough to illustrate a complexity that can't just be reduced to algorithms run amok. When it comes to explaining the phenomenon of right-wing populism, liberals are likely to argue both that the populist era has exposed a darkness always present at the heart of conservative politics and that a toxic, post-truth new-media ecosystem has greased the skids for President Trump, Brexit and the rest. In the case of white-identitarian media personalities popular on YouTube, the two arguments converge.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But in the profiles you can also see clear illustrations of two arguments that a certain kind of conservative \u2014 the kind who locate their politics somewhere between the Trumpians and the Resistance \u2014 is likely to offer in response to liberalism's explanations. First, that populism is a reaction to the breakdown of community outside the liberal metropole, a breakdown that the fiscally conservative-socially liberal \"centrism\" of our leaders has worsened or left unaddressed. And second, that far-right personalities attract people by offering an escape from the airlessness of liberalism, a chance to rebel against its <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2016/09/21/opinion/campaign-stops/clintons-samantha-bee-problem.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">cultural hegemony</a> and <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/25/opinion/sunday/how-liberalism-loses.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">increasing ideological conformism</a>.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Caleb Cain, Roose's subject, illustrates the first argument, to the extent that he seems like a character from the pages of Charles Murray's \"Coming Apart\" or Tim Carney's \"Alienated America\" or J.D. Vance's \"Hillbilly Elegy,\" to cite just the most prominent right-leaning authors who have written about lower-middle-class decay:</p><blockquote class=\"css-scfbvi etf134l0\"><p class=\"css-ma92ss evys1bk0\">The internet was an escape. Mr. Cain grew up in postindustrial Appalachia and was raised by his conservative Christian grandparents. He was smart, but shy and socially awkward, and he carved out an identity during high school as a countercultural punk. He went to community college, but dropped out after three semesters.</p><p class=\"css-ma92ss evys1bk0\">Broke and depressed, he resolved to get his act together. He began looking for help in the same place he looked for everything: YouTube.</p></blockquote><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In other words, a story about the internet is also a story about the attenuation of non-online forms of community, about fatherlessness and family breakdown, about the travails of the \"some college\" demographic, about the social crisis of coal country and the Rust Belt. And it's therefore an example of why attempts to wall off explanations for populism into mutually exclusive \"economic anxiety\" and \"racism\" categories are so futile: There is an <em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">integrated</em> relationship between socioeconomic conditions in downscale America and the appeal of redpilled YouTube, between changing personal and material conditions and the appeal of virtual white-identitarian \"community.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">There is also an integrated relationship between how elite liberalism has evolved and the kind of reactions it provokes. Here is the opening act, from the Washingtonian profile, of the suburban-D.C. episode that sent its 13-year-old subject into the online wilds in search of support and solidarity:</p><blockquote class=\"css-scfbvi etf134l0\"><p class=\"css-ma92ss evys1bk0\">One morning during first period, a male friend of Sam's mentioned a meme whose suggestive name was an inside joke between the two of them. Sam laughed. A girl at the table overheard their private conversation, misconstrued it as a sexual reference, and reported it as sexual harassment. Sam's guidance counselor pulled him out of his next class and accused him of \"breaking the law.\" Before long, he was in the office of a male administrator who informed him that the exchange was \"illegal,\" hinted that the police were coming, and delivered him into the custody of the school's resource officer. At the administrator's instruction, that man ushered Sam into an empty room, handed him a blank sheet of paper, and instructed him to write a \"statement of guilt.\"</p><p class=\"css-ma92ss evys1bk0\">No one called me as this unfolded, even though Sam cried for about six hours straight as staff members parked him in vacant offices to keep him away from other students. When he stepped off the bus that afternoon and I asked why his eyes were so swollen, he informed me that he would probably be suspended, but possibly also expelled and arrested.</p><p class=\"css-ma92ss evys1bk0\">\\u2026 In an out-of-body moment, I imagined that this very episode would be cited by some future cultural critic on the limits of liberalism \\u2026</p></blockquote><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">And yes, perhaps too predictably, here I am citing it \u2014 as a particularly vivid example, from inside the D.C. bubble, of how progressivism fosters alienation and potential rebellion long before any sinister Silicon Valley algorithms get involved. And, going further, as an example of how the alt-right's promise of \"secret knowledge\" about gender, race and sexuality finds a ready audience among young people primed by aspects of their own progressive education to suspect that the system is enforcing ideology rather than imparting truth.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Which, let me stress again, doesn't mean that the far-right YouTubers are actually good or the algorithms actually benign. Nor does it mean that conservatives reacting to liberal critiques of YouTube should automatically leap to the defense of either \u2014 on the assumption that as goes the YouTube success of Stefan Molyneux, so goes the non-racist right.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Yes, it's understandable for conservatives to worry that if Silicon Valley censors the likes of Molyneux, it will end up censoring them. It's sensible for them to join parts in the left in worrying about the concentrated power over information that the stewards of social-media platforms enjoy. And it's necessary for them to recognize that the influence of redpillers and white-identitarians reflects their own failure, across the decades of movement-conservative institution building, to create something that seems more compelling to fugitives from liberalism than the Spirit of the Reddit Thread.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">With all that said, though, a humane conservatism should still be able to thrive in a world where white nationalists have trouble monetizing their extremism, in which YouTube algorithms are built to maximize something other than addiction. And the endpoint of both the Times and Washingtonian profiles, in which personal contact with real-life alt-righters and counterarguments from online left-wingers suffice to pull the main characters away from the far right, suggests that the current Very Online alternative to liberalism is not necessarily built to last.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But if conservatives would be unwise to commit themselves to the defense of some inalienable right to sell crackpottery on YouTube, liberals would be equally unwise to focus so intently on the algorithm, and to pour so much energy into pressuring Silicon Valley to build a better, more progressive way of steering their readers through the information sea.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Whatever role the structure of the internet plays in radicalization, the root causes are still primarily sociological and political, and they will perdure and manifest themselves somewhere, somehow, no matter what YouTube suggests for your next video when you watch a Milton Friedman lecture.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Moreover, there is no better example of the technocratic spirit's moral idiocy than the idea that, with a social crisis in the hinterland and ideological calcification at the heart of educated power, what we need is a better <em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">algorithm</em> to prevent people \u2014 young men, especially \u2014 from getting too restless or rebellious or extreme.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The healing of the body politic will not be accomplished with such fiddling. There may be left-wing or liberal solutions to our deeper problems. But an elite that tries to manage them away with more enlightened media curation deserves to inherit nothing but the wind.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1bmqgre epkadsg3\"><div class=\"css-13ft82o epkadsg0\">Politics and culture</div><div class=\"css-15g2oxy epkadsg2\"><div class=\"css-4q4vfu e16ij5yr6\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/08/opinion/euthanasia-netherlands-noa-pothoven.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedLinks&amp;pgtype=Article\"><div class=\"css-i9gxme e16ij5yr4\"><div class=\"css-11jd139 e16ij5yr2\">Opinion | Ross Douthat: The Politics of Dystopia</div><time class=\"css-rqb9bm e16638kd0\" datetime=\"2019-06-08\">June 8, 2019</time></div><div class=\"css-77hcv e16ij5yr0\"></div></a></div></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">The Times is committed to publishing </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/31/opinion/letters/letters-to-editor-new-york-times-women.html\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">a diversity of letters</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\"> to the editor. We'd like to hear what you think about this or any of our articles. Here are some </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://help.nytimes.com/hc/en-us/articles/115014925288-How-to-submit-a-letter-to-the-editor\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">tips</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">. And here's our email: </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"mailto:letters@nytimes.com\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">letters@nytimes.com</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">.</em></p><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">Follow The New York Times Opinion section on </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.facebook.com/nytopinion\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">Facebook</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">, </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://twitter.com/NYTOpinion\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">Twitter (@NYTOpinion)</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\"> and </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.instagram.com/nytopinion/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">Instagram</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">, join the Facebook political discussion group, </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.facebook.com/groups/votingwhilefemale/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">Voting While Female</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">.</em></p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/11/opinion/youtube-radicalization-algorithms.html#commentsContainer", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">Opinion | The Faults Beyond Our Algorithms - The New York Times</title>"}, "nyc-taxi-medallion-suicides-the-weekly": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><h2 class=\"css-ani50b eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-40ce58ce\">Episode 2: The Myth of the Medallion</h2><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Producer/Director </strong>Suzanne Hillinger</p><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\">Join the conversation about The Times's new TV show with @theweekly on <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://twitter.com/theweekly\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Twitter</a> and <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.instagram.com/theweekly/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Instagram</a>. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"></p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">How does a New York City taxi driver who makes about $22,000 a year get a loan for almost $1 million? <!-- -->Our reporters investigating the taxi industry for \"The Weekly\" found that <!-- -->a group of under-regulated industry leaders created a financial bubble in the market for medallions, the permits that let drivers own their own cab. Bankers, brokers, fleet owners and even city officials artificially inflated the prices of medallions and reaped huge profits by steering immigrant drivers into reckless loans.</p><h3 class=\"css-1gx894m e1gnsphs0\" id=\"link-8f5d1aa\">The Fallout<span class=\"css-8l6xbc evw5hdy0\"> </span></h3><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">After The Times first published its investigation in May 2019, various government officials vowed to take action. </p><ul class=\"css-1xx6m9o ez3869y0\"><li class=\"css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0\"><p class=\"css-15hwz5e evys1bk0\">The city is investigating the brokers.</p></li><li class=\"css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0\"><p class=\"css-15hwz5e evys1bk0\">The state has begun an inquiry into the lenders.</p></li></ul><ul class=\"css-1xx6m9o ez3869y0\"><li class=\"css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0\"><p class=\"css-15hwz5e evys1bk0\">The <!-- -->federal government<!-- --> is reviewing some of the regulators.</p></li></ul><hr class=\"css-16zlh5b e1mu4ftr0\"/><h3 class=\"css-1gx894m e1gnsphs0\" id=\"link-17f7cd22\">Featured Reporters<span class=\"css-8l6xbc evw5hdy0\"> </span></h3></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div><div class=\"css-7t70i5\"><div class=\"css-17pke92\"><div class=\"css-1i18ghh\"><div class=\"css-ygtapu\"><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/05/universal/the-weekly-brian-headshot/the-weekly-brian-headshot-square320-v2.jpg\"/></div></div><div class=\"css-k4qa62\"><p class=\"css-15ngikh evys1bk0\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Brian M. Rosentha</strong>l is an investigative reporter on the Metro Desk. A Pulitzer Prize-winning journalist, he uses data, documents and interviews to expose problems in New York. He's most passionate about telling the stories of vulnerable people in society. Follow Brian on Twitter: <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://twitter.com/brianmrosenthal\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">@brianmrosenthal</a></p></div></div></div></div><div><div class=\"css-7t70i5\"><div class=\"css-17pke92\"><div class=\"css-1i18ghh\"><div class=\"css-ygtapu\"><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/04/universal/the-weekly-emma/the-weekly-emma-square320-v4.jpg\"/></div></div><div class=\"css-k4qa62\"><p class=\"css-15ngikh evys1bk0\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Emma G. Fitzsimmons </strong>covers transportation for the Metro desk. She writes about the ways New Yorkers get around the city \u2014 above and below ground. Her reporting has focused on the decline of mass transit and the rapid rise of ride-hailing apps like Uber. Follow Emma on Twitter: <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://twitter.com/emmagf\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">@emmgf</a></p></div></div></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"></p><h3 class=\"css-1gx894m e1gnsphs0\" id=\"link-611f0f8b\">#TheWeeklyNYT </h3><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Mohammad Hossain, one of the drivers featured in the show, and his family watched the episode with Brian and Suzanne at Times headquarters. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-cfo9c3\"></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">After the episode, Emma called cabby Nicolae Hent, who lost his fellow colleague and friend to suicide last year. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-cfo9c3\"></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><h3 class=\"css-1gx894m e1gnsphs0\" id=\"link-48d86eca\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Where Are They Now? </strong></h3><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\">Brian, Emma, and Suzanne give us the latest update on the people you saw on this episode of \"The Weekly.\" </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-nvxo42 e73j0it0\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-17bnq82 e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/09/universal/09-theweekly-mohammad2/7069aad8ef2b47269b2de247b90b7c3f-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:217.82222222222222px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l6g02d e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\"><strong>Mohammad Hossain</strong> is still driving his cab and struggling to pay the $700,000 left on his loan. With his medallion worth only about $150,000, he hopes that the city will help him and other drivers reach a deal with their banks.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Adam Beckman for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-17bnq82 e1g7ppur0\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:217.82222222222222px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l6g02d e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\"><strong>Richard Feinsilver</strong>, a bankruptcy lawyer who represents hundreds of taxi medallion owners, says at least 250 of his clients have filed for bankruptcy.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Adam Beckman for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div><div class=\"css-nvxo42 e73j0it0\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-17bnq82 e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/09/universal/09-theweekly-taxi-show-notes-nicholae-hent/ec8cf90e268d4c2b90e9209197e535d6-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:217.82222222222222px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l6g02d e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span He stays in touch with the family of his friend, Nicanor Ochisor, who took his own life last year.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Dave Waldron for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-17bnq82 e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/09/universal/09-theweekly-coreyjohnson/3489a2e746194d8f8ecb41b28bb11bb0-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:217.82222222222222px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l6g02d e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\"><strong>Corey Johnson</strong>, New York City Council speaker, says the Council plans to hold hearings on ways to help the taxi industry and will appoint members to a new task force.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Andreas Burgess for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"></p><h3 class=\"css-1gx894m e1gnsphs0\" id=\"link-5ab28b31\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">What Can You Do to Help? </strong></h3><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">State and city leaders are <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/20/nyregion/nyc-taxi-medallion-loans-attorney-general.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">investigating the taxi crisis</a> and discussing several different solutions to help drivers, including a bailout of their loans and changing how the loans are regulated. Some lawmakers are <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.cityandstateny.com/articles/policy/infrastructure/how-new-york-could-respond-to-taxi-medallion-lending-crisis.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">crafting legislation</a> to address issues identified by the Times investigation.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Several city councilmembers say the city should take responsibility for its role in driving medallion sales. They are working on a bill that would allow the city to buy medallion loans from lenders and forgive much of the debt.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">New Yorkers often ask Emma Fitzsimmons, the transit reporter for The Times, how they can help taxi drivers and if they should delete Uber or Lyft, the popular ride-hail apps. It's a complicated issue, she said, and there's no easy answer. But one thing definitely helps: Tip your driver.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Whether you hail a taxi or order an Uber, your driver often works long hours and spends a lot on expenses such as gas and insurance. Taxi and app drivers are both <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/17/nyregion/uber-taxi-drivers-struggle.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">struggling financially</a>. The <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/10/02/travel/should-you-tip-your-uber-driver-if-so-how-much.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">tip goes directly to drivers</a> and helps them support their families. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1l6nq8w\" style=\"margin:0 auto\"><div class=\"medium css-17dprlf\" data-id=\"100000006432889\" \"difficult to be discreet\" with a camera crew following her around. \"When we went to the taxi lot at JFK Airport, suddenly I was surrounded by drivers, all wanting to share their story.\"</p></span></div><span class=\"css-2hd72h e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Suzanne Hillinger for The New York Times</span></span></div></div></div></li><li aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"css-pwuqn0 false\" data-carousel-item=\"list-item\" id=\"U2xpZGVzaG93Om55dDovL3NsaWRlc2hvdy9kZjEwYjkyNi1jOGNlLTU4OTItYWQ0NC00OGMwYjEzZWZlNDE=-2\"><div class=\"css-1kcsu6r\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"layoutHorizontal css-1s800kr toneNews\" class=\"css-17ai7jg emkp2hg0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"emkp2hg2 css-1nwzsjy e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span><span class=\"css-1dv1kvn\">Credit</span><span>Kholood Eid for The New York Times</span></span></span></figcaption></figure></div><div class=\"css-1v52nlq\"><div class=\"css-s2ruro\"><div class=\"css-1jq68ls\"><div class=\"css-64utwb\" data-carousel-item=\"list-item-caption\"><span class=\"css-cubd73 e13ogyst0\"><p>New York City issued the first taxi medallions in 1937 for $10 apiece. For decades, their value slowly climbed. Then, between 2002 and 2014, the price skyrocketed \u2014 from $200,000 dollars to $1.2 million. The medallion was seen as a safe investment, but the truth is, many people who spread the myth of the medallion had an incentive for the prices to go up forever.\\xa0</p></span></div><span class=\"css-2hd72h e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Kholood Eid for The New York Times</span></span></div></div></div></li><li aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"css-pwuqn0 false\" data-carousel-item=\"list-item\" id=\"U2xpZGVzaG93Om55dDovL3NsaWRlc2hvdy9kZjEwYjkyNi1jOGNlLTU4OTItYWQ0NC00OGMwYjEzZWZlNDE=-3\"><div class=\"css-1kcsu6r\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"layoutHorizontal css-1s800kr toneNews\"
