600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/07/universal/the-weekly-taxi-bts-fisher/60174197441d4fa08b36db3696bb0810-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/07/universal/the-weekly-taxi-bts-fisher/60174197441d4fa08b36db3696bb0810-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w\"/></div><figcaption class=\"css-17ai7jg emkp2hg0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"emkp2hg2 css-1nwzsjy e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span><span class=\"css-1dv1kvn\">Credit</span><span>Kholood Eid for The New York Times</span></span></span></figcaption></figure></div><div class=\"css-1v52nlq\"><div class=\"css-s2ruro\"><div class=\"css-1jq68ls\"><div class=\"css-64utwb\" data-carousel-item=\"list-item-caption\"><span class=\"css-cubd73 e13ogyst0\"><p>Larry Fisher was a chief loan officer at Melrose Credit Union, a major taxi lender, from 2003 \u2014 2016. At the height of the bubble, the company collected $80 million in interest and fees every year. Mr. Fisher said, \"So many people have gone bankrupt\\u2026 I feel badly about it, but what has kept me sane is that I'm not the only one who was involved.\"</p></span></div><span class=\"css-2hd72h e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Kholood Eid for The New York Times</span></span></div></div></div></li></ul><nav aria-label=\"Slideshow\" class=\"css-15sp14x\"><div class=\"css-tmi0aa\"><span class=\"css-1npeap7\" data-carousel-item=\"slide-counter\">1/4</span></div><button aria-label=\"Previous Slide\" class=\"css-16z6f8n\" data-carousel-item=\"btn-prev\" type=\"button\"><i class=\"css-1dkvdsl e1d7eslp1\"></i></button><button aria-label=\"Next Slide\" class=\"css-16z6f8n\" data-carousel-item=\"btn-next\" type=\"button\"><i class=\"css-1tpdyqu e1d7eslp0\"></i></button></nav></div></section><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><h3 class=\"css-1gx894m e1gnsphs0\" id=\"link-6c9f6f1c\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Complete coverage </strong></h3><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The episode features Brian's investigation of the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/19/nyregion/nyc-taxis-medallions-suicides.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">reckless loans that \"devastated a generation of taxi drivers</a>.\" Taxi medallions were once considered a safe investment. <!-- -->Now they sell for a fraction of the record price.<!-- --> Read parts <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/19/nyregion/nyc-taxis-medallions-suicides.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">one</a> and <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/19/nyregion/taxi-medallions.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">two</a>.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Mohammad emptied his savings to buy a taxi medallion. He had no idea that he had just signed away his financial freedom. Watch this clip of \"The Weekly.\" </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"sizeMedium css-qhlm6o\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/VideoObject\" role=\"group\"><meta content=\"A lot of the medallion owners that we've talked to have filed for bankruptcy. Have you thought about doing that? Yeah. What are you thinking about? Why haven't you, yet? Who me? Yeah. I bought medallion from the city. I think city will help me. You know? I see on the... I know so many drivers they kill themselves. But I have a family. I love my family. So I don't want to kill myself. My life is more important for my family. I love my family, than medallion. So you can't give up for your family? Yeah. On the same day that Mohammad bought his medallion so did 167 other drivers. Since then, 40% of them have filed for bankruptcy. If you look at enough of their loan documents you notice patterns. These drivers signed away their rights, paid huge fees and never came close to settling their debt. While the people they trusted made all the money and shared none of the personal risk. There was the city, which sold the medallions, the brokers who collected commissions and the bankers who wrote the loans and sold some of them for profit. Eventually, you realize that this wasn't by accident. Many insiders knew that the whole thing was a house of cards.\" itemprop=\"transcript\"/><div class=\"css-bsn42l\"><span class=\"css-1dv1kvn\">Video</span><div><div class=\"css-1t0v8sy etkm6pg0\"><div class=\"css-mm3pwi\"></div><div class=\"css-1a74oa6 etkm6pg1\"><div class=\"css-1ihorw etkm6pg2\"><img alt=\"Video player loading\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/06/universal/the-weekly-mohammad-promo-1/e79d304915b84b9d911fc7d1b27d501d-videoSixteenByNineJumbo1600.jpg\"/></div><div class=\"css-1ruigs3\"><div class=\"css-v15h5m\"><div></div><div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-17ai7jg emkp2hg0\" itemprop=\"caption description name\"></figcaption></figure><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><ul class=\"css-1xx6m9o ez3869y0\"><li class=\"css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0\"><p class=\"css-15hwz5e evys1bk0\">It took a year, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/22/reader-center/taxi-medallion-investigation.html?rref=collection%2Fbyline%2Fbrian-m.-rosenthal&amp;action=click&amp;contentCollection=undefined&amp;region=stream&amp;module=stream_unit&amp;version=latest&amp;contentPlacement=1&amp;pgtype=collection\" title=\"\">450 interviews and a database</a> built from scratch to answer a simple question: Why had anyone ever agreed to pay $1 million for the right to drive a yellow cab?</p></li><li class=\"css-o74qhc eoqvrfo0\"><p class=\"css-15hwz5e evys1bk0\">Emma reports on the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/12/02/nyregion/taxi-drivers-suicide-nyc.html\" title=\"\">suicides of several New York City taxi drivers</a>. She breaks down what the city's taxi commissioner, Meera Joshi, characterizes as an epidemic. </p><p class=\"css-15hwz5e evys1bk0\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">If you are having thoughts of suicide, call the National Suicide Prevention Lifeline at 1-800-273-8255 (TALK) or go to </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.speakingofsuicide.com/resources\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">SpeakingOfSuicide.com/resources</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\"> for a list of additional resources. Here's what you can do when a loved one is severely depressed.</em></p></li></ul><hr class=\"css-16zlh5b e1mu4ftr0\"/><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Director of Photography</strong> Adam Beckman<br/><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Video Editor</strong> Pierre Takal<br/><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Story Editors </strong>Dan Barry, Liz O. Baylen, Liz Day, Alexandra Garcia<br/><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">Associate Producer</strong> Madeline Rosenberg </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/07/the-weekly/nyc-taxi-medallion-suicides-the-weekly.html", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">The Weekly - Now on Hulu - How NYC Taxi Drivers Bought Medallions and Became Victims of a Reckless Lending Scheme - The New York Times</title>"}, "astrology-occult-millennials": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">We're living in the middle of a religious revival; it's just that the movements that are rising are not what we normally call \"religion.\" The first rising movement is astrology. According to a <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2018/10/01/new-age-beliefs-common-among-both-religious-and-nonreligious-americans/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">2018 Pew poll</a>, 29 percent of Americans say they believe in astrology. That's more than are members of mainline Protestant churches.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">This surge in belief is primarily among the young. According to a <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nsf.gov/statistics/2018/nsb20181/assets/404/science-and-technology-public-attitudes-and-understanding_atables.pdf\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">National Science Foundation survey</a>, 44 percent of 18- to 24-year-olds say that astrology is somewhat or very \"scientific.\" Unsurprisingly, online horoscope sites are booming. Stella Bugbee, editor of The Cut, told <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2018/01/the-new-age-of-astrology/550034/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">The Atlantic</a> that in 2017 the typical horoscope got 150 percent more traffic than it had the year before.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Another surging spiritual movement is witchcraft. In 1990, only 8,000 Americans self-identified as Wiccans. Ten years later there were 134,000, and today, along with other neo-pagans, there are over a million. As Tara Isabella Burton put it in an excellent, deeply researched <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.the-american-interest.com/2019/06/07/the-rise-of-progressive-occultism/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">essay</a> in The American Interest, \"Wicca, by that estimation, is technically the fastest-growing religion in America.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The third great rising spiritual force is mindfulness, which seems to be everywhere. The fourth is wokeness, what some have called the Great Awokening. Burton's essay is really about how astrology and witchcraft have become important spiritual vocabularies within parts of the social justice movement. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In March, she wrote, Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez shared her birth time with the astrologer Arthur Lipp-Bonewits, who then shared her birth chart with the world, creating an online sensation. \"AOC's Aries Moon indicates that she's emotionally fed by a certain amount of independence, self-determination, and spontaneity,\" Jeanna Kadlec <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.allure.com/story/alexandria-ocasio-cortez-astrology-birth-chart-reading\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">wrote</a> in Allure.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">During the Kavanaugh hearings, 13,000 \"resistance witches\" cast a hex on Brett Kavanaugh. There is now a plethora of guidebooks for how to use astrology and witchcraft to advance left-wing causes. They have names like <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.llewellyn.com/product.php?ean=9780738759968\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">\"Magic for Resistance: Rituals and Spells for Change\"</a> and <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://revelore.press/product/the-new-aradia-a-witchs-handbook-to-magical-resistance/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">\"The New Aradia: A Witch's Handbook to Magical Resistance.\"</a> </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">These surging movements are people's attempts to solve the major needs of the current moment.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The first need is simply to find a way to be spiritual. People are always saying we live in a more secular age, but secularism never really comes. Humans are transcendent creatures who have spiritual experiences and instinctively appeal to supernatural powers. Even in the most secular parts of society, there is great and unfulfilled spiritual yearning.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Second, there is a widespread need to slow down, to escape the pace of life technology wants and to live at a human pace.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Third, there is a widespread need to express alienation. Interest in the occult rises during periods of transition and disillusion. It happened in the late 1960s, and it's happening today. For many, the traditional organized religions are implicated in the existing power structures. Being occult is a way to announce that you stand on the fringe of society, that you stand against the patriarchy, against the heteronormative culture and against the structures of oppression. Political alienation manifests itself in the alt-right and the energized radical left. It makes sense that it would manifest itself in the spiritual realm, too.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Fourth is the need for identity markers. We live at a time when many of the traditional sources of identity (ethnicity, rooted neighborhood) are being erased. Astrology tells you who you are and what traits you have. In a highly diverse society, it also tells you what sort of people you're likely to be compatible and incompatible with. When I hear people talk about astrology, this is how they are<!-- --> using it.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Fifth is the desire to live within a coherent creed and community, but without having that creed impinge on your individual autonomy. Being an Orthodox Jew is a thick but binding life. The emerging spirituality is a hodgepodge spirituality. Each person borrows practices from, say, Native American, Buddhist, Christian, Jewish and SoulCycle traditions and blends them in a way he or she finds moving. There is no grand narrative, no specific way one is expected to live, no <!-- -->set of laws you have to obey or even a<!-- --> specific cult leader who might boss you around. Religion bows before individualism.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Finally, many people seem to want to be alternative without actually leaving the mainstream world. The people I know who talk about astrology sort of believe it, but they sort of don't. Their attitude is ironical, attached and detached all at once.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Even the occultists are not really that countercultural. For example, David Salisbury's book <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://redwheelweiser.com/detail.html?id=9781578636570\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">\"Witchcraft Activism: A Toolkit for Magical Resistance\"</a> is surprisingly normal. Salisbury gives standard advice on how to be an activist. It's just that he asks you to say a prayer to Hermes, the messenger god, when you send an important email.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">I doubt that much of this will be sustainable. I doubt it's possible to have tight community and also total autonomy, that it's possible to detach spiritual practices from the larger narratives and cultures and still have something life-shaping. But society is groaning. New forms are coming into being. We really are living through a moment of major transitional change.</p><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">The Times is committed to publishing </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/31/opinion/letters/letters-to-editor-new-york-times-women.html\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">a diversity of letters</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\"> to the editor. We'd like to hear what you think about this or any of our articles. Here are some </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://help.nytimes.com/hc/en-us/articles/115014925288-How-to-submit-a-letter-to-the-editor\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">tips</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">. And here's our email: </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"mailto:letters@nytimes.com\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">letters@nytimes.com</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">.</em></p><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">Follow The New York Times Opinion section on </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.facebook.com/nytopinion\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">Facebook</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">, </em><a 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/04/fashion/04SOHO-WELLNESS-Showfields-slide/merlin_155249514_8be5edd0-2305-4caf-8a70-91991d785ac0-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w\"/></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Dina Auslander rides a slide at Showfields, which houses many pop-up stores in SoHo.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Jeenah Moon for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Within a half-mile radius in downtown Manhattan, there are five matcha stores: MatchaBar, Matchaful, Cha Cha Matcha, the other Cha Cha Matcha and Matcha n' More, which are each less than five minutes apart on foot. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Matcha, a kind of powdered green tea used in Japanese tea ceremonies, has become a popular drink in the wellness scene for its grassy green color and antioxidants. High-end cafes in SoHo like Matchaful blend it with nut milks or spices and sell it for $7, more than the cost of a latte.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">At the same time, places that once catered to health-minded New Yorkers before wellness became a buzzword \u2014 spots like <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/15/dining/souen-nyc-closing.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">Souen</a>, Integral Yoga Natural Foods and Angelica Kitchen \u2014 are closing. All three opened in the 1970s, when SoHo was home to an artistic and creative community.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/04/fashion/04SOHO-WELLNESS-matcha/merlin_155249583_ae3412cd-cd9f-4089-a31b-1d852b020f5b-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Matcha from Coffee 'n Clothes.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Jeenah Moon for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In the 1960s and '70s, the neighborhood was a magnet for artists. Then came fancy shops and French restaurants. Most young artists haven't been able to afford to live or maintain studios there for the last couple of decades.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Instead there is By Chloe, a vegan fast food restaurant, which sells a quinoa taco salad for $12.45; Brodo, which sells cups of bone broth for $10; the Good Market, which sells pineapple raspberry kombucha organic slushies for $4.50; Welleco and the Nue Co, both supplement stores; the Hemp Garden, where CBD sheet masks sell for $29.99; the Detox Market, where the Vintner's Daughter Active Treatment Essence face oil is $225; Lululemon and Nike; boutique fitness establishments like Y-7, New York Pilates (three locations), SLT and SoulCycle, where classes are upward of $30.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In early April, Kind, the snack food company, organized a two-day pop-up highlighting its \"Sweeteners Uncovered\" campaign, which shows hidden sugars in popular snack foods.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/04/fashion/04SOHO-WELLNESS-sustain/merlin_155153322_6096d5ed-aca1-4a42-b88a-34db7f6005d7-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:288.71111111111117px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">The Sustain pop-up, with a neon art display.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Mirra Studio</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">This took the form of a high-tech bodega at 579 Broadway, a space that once housed an Aldo shoe store and whose rent for the space Kind declined to share. At the pop-up, the sugar content from Kind's competitors could be revealed by scanning a QR code. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Some of the few dozen people there bypassed the nutritional information to stuff free plastic fanny packs with free Kind Bars. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The company hosted a pop-up in Times Square two years ago, but Jenna <!-- -->Keplesky<!-- -->, who works in Kind's communications department, lobbied to move this one to SoHo. \"I was encouraging locations that were more cost effective, but Jenna wanted the right brand message,\" said Daniel Lubetzky, the chief executive of Kind. \"I do think there's a sense that SoHo is more representative and ahead of the curve in health and wellness in New York City.\" </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The neighborhood is also known to have a steady stream of foot traffic from New Yorkers and tourists alike, Ms. Keplesky said.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In many cases, fanciful and high-concept pop-ups have followed wellness retailers to SoHo and its surrounding streets.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Blume, which sells self-care and menstrual products marketed to young women and teenagers, had a pop-up at <!-- -->224 Mulberry Street<!-- --> in NoLIta in February that included a slumber party and panel discussion. The founders, Taran and Bunny Ghatrora, wrote in an email that they chose the location because it is one of their favorite neighborhoods and that a large portion of their New York community is based there.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-i67pzw e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/04/fashion/04SOHO-WELLNESS-buffy/04SOHO-WELLNESS-buffy-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:471.73333333333335px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">A visitor kicks back at the Buffy pop-up.</span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The condom company Sustain Natural hosted the Get on Top Pop-Up in April 2018 at 208 Bowery, with neon vulva art installations and tampon-filled bathtubs leading into a back event space called the womb. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Meika Hollender, its chief executive, said that foot traffic and a neighborhood affinity for wellness made her choose the Bowery: \"There are so many like-minded wellness studios and brands showcasing their products in this area that it felt like a natural opportunity to reach consumers in a fun and accessible way. I mean, who wouldn't be curious walking past a vagina-themed pop-up.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Buffy, which makes comforters out of recycled plastic bottles and eucalyptus plants, had a \"physical touch-point\" called Soft-Space at 150 Wooster Street (where, last year, a penthouse sold for $32.6 million) during the 2018 holiday season. According to a news release for the company, inspiration came from Buckminster Fuller and the hippie modernist movement of the 1960s and '70s.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Clean Market, a store on 54th Street and Second Avenue that sells natural beauty products and services like vitamin IV drips, has a pop-up in NoLIta at Project by Equinox on <!-- -->Mulberry Street<!-- -->. \"We want the downtown crowd to get to know us,\" said the founder Lily Kunin one afternoon as she sent an associate on an errand a few blocks north to the Farmer's Dog pop-up at Showfields at 11 Bond Street. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/04/fashion/04SOHO-WELLNESS-showfields/merlin_155249577_2acf1c95-85aa-4a6c-8ad8-b9d099d1fdbf-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">An exterior view of Showfields.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Jeenah Moon for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Currently Showfields has pop-ups decorated with potted plants and pink velveteen chairs from the Australian skin care brand Frank Body and Quip, a dental company that frequently advertises on podcasts. <!-- -->The<!-- --> cafe, called Coffee 'n Clothes, sells miniature cupcakes and lattes emblazoned with the logos of fashion brands. (Showfields, which calls itself \"the Most Interesting Store in the World,\" occupies a 1913 NoHo building that, before its purchase in 2015 by FRF Realty for $26 million, housed a 43-bed women's shelter.)</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Despite the fact that the <!-- -->store<!-- --> was virtually empty on a recent Monday afternoon, some tenants, who pay a flat fee for space, are pleased with early results. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"What we've managed to do in sales in three weeks was greater in total than one of our retail partners who has 13 or 14 doors nationwide,\" said Jasmina Aganovic, the founder of Mother Dirt, a skin care line in Boston that has a second-floor space at Showfields. \"It's a sexy location in New York City, and we have a large concentration of customers in New York and Brooklyn in particular.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Large companies have used wellness businesses as destinations for their own events. OtterBox introduced its Otter &amp; Pop phone cases to press at Chillhouse, a cafe, nail salon and massage studio on the neighboring Lower East Side. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/04/fashion/04SOHO-WELLNESS-mother-dirt/merlin_155249490_3a2e10c8-6c7c-4903-b77d-6c8277def66b-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Mother Dirt mist products.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Jeenah Moon for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Landlords are enthusiastic about wellness-related tenants, according to Paul Wexler, the head of Wexler Healthcare Properties at the Corcoran Group. \"Landlords are generally encouraged by it,\" he said. \"It's a way to fill retail spaces, and an amenity to their buildings. There are spaces we're marketing with that in mind.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Some smaller wellness businesses are looking to spread brand awareness if they could only find the right space. Justine Monsul, the founder of Monfefo, a beverage company that makes organic pressed ginger and turmeric shots, has been looking for a pop-up storefront. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Trying to find a place in New York is like winning the lottery,\" she said on the phone during a trip to Israel. \"I want to share my story and have more of a relationship to my customers. You don't just want a store, you want an experience. You want some palo santo burning.\" </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Colette Dong, the co-founder and C.E.O. of the Ness, opened a pop-up trampoline workout studio in nearby TriBeCa in a location that was a Bikram yoga studio. The pop-up lease was \"a way to get our feet wet without getting locked into a five- or 10-year lease term and test the demand for it,\" Ms. Dong said.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Will we even have studios in five years?\" Ms. Dong said. \"Will there be studios to do our online streaming workouts? Will we be working out with robots?\" </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Maybe best not to commit to anything too long-term.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/10/style/self-care/soho-wellness-pop-up.html", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">Has SoHo Become One Big Wellness Pop-Up? - The New York Times</title>"}, "brazil-cuba-doctors-jair-bolsonaro": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">EMBU-GUA\\xc7U, Brazil \u2014 The shiny plastic chairs all sat empty in a public health clinic, and the patients who staggered in were told to come back Thursday \u2014 the only day of the week now when a doctor is there.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">This small Brazilian city, Embu-Gua\\xe7u, home to 70,000 people, recently lost eight of its 18 public-sector doctors, a devastating loss for the city's network of free clinics, forcing hard choices about who gets care and when.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"It's heartbreaking,\" said Fernanda Kimura, a doctor who coordinates the assignment of physicians to the clinics for the local health department. \"Like choosing which child to feed.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The sick and the injured turned away that day in a working-class neighborhood of Embu-Gua\\xe7u represent only a tiny fraction of the estimated 28 million people across Brazil whose access to health care has been sharply curtailed, according to the National Confederation of Municipalities, following a confrontation between Brazil's new president, Jair Bolsonaro, and Cuba.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In November, Cuba announced it was <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/11/14/world/americas/brazil-cuba-doctors-jair-bolsonaro.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">recalling the 8,517 doctors</a> it had deployed to poor and remote regions of Brazil, a response to the tough stance against Cuba that Mr. Bolsonaro had vowed to take when he was elected in October.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The abrupt departure of thousands of doctors has presented Mr. Bolsonaro with one of his first major policy challenges \u2014 and has tested his ability to deliver on a promise to find homegrown substitutions quickly.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors2/merlin_154541484_980a100f-5815-45fa-8875-a64914f95357-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><img alt=\"\" class=\"css-1m50asq\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors2/merlin_154541484_980a100f-5815-45fa-8875-a64914f95357-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" itemprop=\"url\" sizes=\"((min-width: 600px) and (max-width: 1004px)) 84vw, (min-width: 1005px) 80vw, 100vw\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors2/merlin_154541484_980a100f-5815-45fa-8875-a64914f95357-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" srcset=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors2/merlin_154541484_980a100f-5815-45fa-8875-a64914f95357-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors2/merlin_154541484_980a100f-5815-45fa-8875-a64914f95357-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors2/merlin_154541484_980a100f-5815-45fa-8875-a64914f95357-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w\"/></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Patients waiting to see a doctor at a clinic in Embu-Gua\\xe7u. \"Now we end up doing triage all day,\" said Erica Toledo, the head nurse at the Jardim Campestre clinic.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Maira Erlich for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"We are graduating, I am certain, around 20,000 doctors a year, and the trend is to increase that number,\"<a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://agenciabrasil.ebc.com.br/politica/noticia/2018-11/bolsonaro-diz-que-programa-mais-medicos-nao-sera-suspenso\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"> Mr. Bolsonaro said in November</a>. \"We can solve this problem with these doctors.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But six months into his presidential term, which started in January, Brazil is struggling to replace the departed Cuban doctors with Brazilian ones: 3,847 public-sector medical positions in almost 3,000 municipalities remained unfilled as of April, according to the most recent figures available.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"In several states, health clinics and their patients don't have doctors,\" said Ligia Bahia, a professor at the Federal University of Rio de Janeiro. \"It's a step backward. It impedes early diagnoses, the monitoring of children, pregnancies and the continuation of treatments that were already underway.\"</p><h2 class=\"css-ani50b eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-57201190\">'Our Cuban brothers will be freed'</h2><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">During his campaign for the presidency, Mr. Bolsonaro, a right-wing populist, committed to making major changes to the Mais M\\xe9dicos program, an initiative begun in 2013 when a leftist government was in power. The program sent doctors into Brazil's small towns, indigenous villages and violent, low-income urban neighborhoods.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">About half of the Mais M\\xe9dicos doctors were from Cuba, and they were deployed to 34 remote indigenous villages and the poorer quarters of more than 4,000 towns and cities, places that established Brazilian physicians largely shun.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"The willingness of Cuban doctors to work in difficult conditions became a cornerstone of the public health system,\" said Ms. Bahia, the professor.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Brazil paid millions of dollars a month to Cuba for the doctors, making them <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/03/17/world/americas/venezuela-cuban-doctors.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">a vital export for the island's coffers</a>. But most of the money went directly to Cuba's Communist government, an arrangement Mr. Bolsonaro warned he would change.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors5/merlin_147216993_0f745f54-8f72-4ee2-aada-7e26538f1435-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:267.44444444444446px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">A group of Cuban doctors who returned to Cuba in November waiting to meet the island's president, Miguel Diaz-Canel.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Desmond Boylan/Associated Press</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Cuban doctors <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/29/world/americas/brazil-cuban-doctors-revolt.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">have long complained about getting only a small cut</a> of the money for their work, and Mr. Bolsonaro said they would have to be allowed to keep their entire salaries and to bring their families with them to Brazil. They would also have to pass equivalency exams to prove their qualifications.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Our Cuban brothers will be freed,\" Mr. Bolsonaro said in an official campaign proposal presented to electoral authorities. \"Their families will be allowed to migrate to Brazil. And, if they pass the revalidation, they will begin to receive the entire amount that was being robbed by the Cuban dictators!\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Two weeks after Mr. Bolsonaro <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/10/28/world/americas/jair-bolsonaro-brazil-election.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">won the presidency in October</a>, Cuba ordered all its doctors out.</p><h2 class=\"css-ani50b eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-19ffaa23\">37,000 young children at risk of death</h2><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Access to free health care is a right under Brazilian law, and Mais M\\xe9dicos was enacted in 2013 by President Dilma Rousseff in a bid to provide medical care to communities that were not being served by the public health system. Through a network of free clinics, the program provided 60 million Brazilians with access to a family doctor in their community for the first time.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In the first four years of Mais M\\xe9dicos, the percentage of Brazilians receiving primary care rose to 70 percent from 59.6 percent, according to<a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.paho.org/bra/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=5809:opas-lanca-relatorio-30-anos-de-sus-que-sus-para-2030-e-destaca-importancia-de-atencao-primaria-e-mais-medicos&amp;Itemid=843\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\"> a report</a> by the Pan-American Health Organization, which coordinated Cuba's participation in the program.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The withdrawal of Cuban doctors could reverse that trend, with the consequences especially severe for those under 5, potentially leading to the deaths of up to 37,000 young children by 2030, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.terra.com.br/vida-e-estilo/saude/saida-de-cubanos-pode-levar-a-aumento-de-37-mil-mortes-diz-opas,c9da3a2fd30f623b7f4a90f607913279de24ust3.html\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">warned Dr. Gabriel Vivas</a>, an official with the Pan-American Health Organization.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In February, it looked as if Mr. Bolsonaro would fulfill his promise: the national Health Ministry announced that all of the positions left vacant by Cuba's withdrawal had been filled with Brazilian doctors. But by April, thousands of the new recruits had either quit or failed to show up for work in the first place.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">More than 2,000 Cuban doctors have chosen to remain in Brazil, defying the call to return home. But with the special arrangement with Cuba terminated, they are now ineligible to practice medicine until they pass an exam \u2014 which the Brazilian government has not offered since 2017 and for which the Health Ministry has set no date.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Luiz Henrique Mandetta, Brazil's health minister, said the new government was working on a bill to ensure the goals of Mais M\\xe9dicos were achieved and the doctors replaced.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Even if the program has various problems, it has a positive side, which is, precisely, diminishing the inequality in health care neglect,\" he said.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But Mr. Mandetta initially said the bill would be sent to Congress between April and May. Now, the ministry says it will be introduced by the end of June.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Karel S\\xe1nchez was one of four Cuban doctors sent to the remote region of Cachoeira do Arari in the Brazilian Amazon. He waited there for five months after his government ordered the withdrawal of all Cuban doctors, with the expectation that Mr. Bolsonaro would respect his campaign pledge to provide an exam so he could continue to work and receive his full salary.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors3/merlin_154676034_14357612-6b3b-41f2-a5a5-16fd97eb9675-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:258.4222222222222px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Dr. Karel S\\xe1nchez decided not to return to Cuba, expecting to be able to keep working in Brazil after taking a revalidation exam. That has not been the case.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Maira Erlich for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"I was happy when Bolsonaro said he wouldn't support a dictatorship,\" Dr. S\\xe1nchez said.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In April, Dr. S\\xe1nchez gave up and moved to S\\xe3o Paulo, where he scrapes together money by selling homemade sweets and working as a baggage handler at an airport.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Now he doesn't talk about us at all, just silence,\" Dr. S\\xe1nchez said.</p><h2 class=\"css-ani50b eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-34971054\">'I told people to think about that before they voted'</h2><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In Embu-Gua\\xe7u, Dr. Santa Cobas, the Cuban doctor who had been serving residents at the clinic now only open on Thursdays, was still nearby and eager to work.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But Dr. Cobas is unemployed, and the 4,000 people she once cared for don't have access to a local doctor six days a week.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Now we end up doing triage all day \u2014 deciding who needs to rush to another hospital, who gets to see the visiting doctor on Thursday and who will just have to wait,\" said Erica Toledo, the head nurse at the clinic, Jardim Campestre, which was opened in 2015.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"Dr. Santa was here from the first day, and it was the first time people felt taken care of by their 'own' doctor,\" Ms. Toledo said. \"They really love her.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The health secretary of Embu-Gua\\xe7u, Dr. Maria Dalva, said she was frustrated that 63 percent of the city had voted for Mr. Bolsonaro, despite his overt antipathy for Mais M\\xe9dicos.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"The child mortality rate here dropped to 7 percent from 17 percent in five years thanks to Mais M\\xe9dicos,\" said Dr. Dalva. \"I told people to think about that before they voted.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/03/world/00brazil-doctors4/merlin_154541490_c1bff55f-4b81-4b61-8d7c-1f8594e74aac-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:258.4222222222222px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">A nurse in an otherwise empty corridor at the clinic in Embu-Gua\\xe7u.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Maira Erlich for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/11/world/americas/brazil-cuba-doctors-jair-bolsonaro.html#commentsContainer", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">Brazil Fails to Replace Cuban Doctors, Hurting Health Care of 28 Million - The New York Times</title>"}, "trump-trade-tariffs": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The events of the past few weeks destroyed whatever credibility Donald Trump may still have had on economic policy. And investors are celebrating. At this point, evidence that Trump tweets are sound and fury signifying nothing is, in effect, good news.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Let's review what happened. First, having gone to great lengths to get a new trade agreement with Mexico and Canada \u2014 an agreement that was very similar to the existing agreement, but one he could slap his own name on \u2014 Trump basically blew up his position by threatening to impose new tariffs unless Mexico did something about border issues that have nothing to do with trade.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">This obviously weakens if it doesn't destroy Trump's ability to negotiate future agreements, on trade or anything else. After all, what's the point of making deals with an administration that reneges on its promises whenever it feels like it?</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But then, barely a week later, Trump called the whole thing off in return for a statement by Mexico that it would do \\u2026 things it had already agreed to <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/08/us/politics/trump-mexico-deal-tariffs.html?rref=collection%2Fbyline%2Fmaggie-haberman&amp;action=click&amp;contentCollection=undefined&amp;region=stream&amp;module=inline&amp;version=latest&amp;contentPlacement=1&amp;pgtype=collection\" title=\"\">months earlier</a>. </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">We don't know exactly what caused Trump to back down, but a good guess is that the warnings of U.S. manufacturers \u2014 horrified at the possibility that Trump's tariff tantrum would disrupt their supply chains \u2014 finally made it through to the Oval Office, or the golf course, or wherever he was when they finally got his ear.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/newsletters/paul-krugman?action=click&amp;module=inline&amp;pgtype=Article\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">[For an even deeper look at what's on Paul Krugman's mind, sign up for his weekly newsletter.]</em></a></p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Now, not having a destructive trade war is a good thing. But what the world learned from this climbdown is that Trump's threats are as empty as his promises.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">An aside: Recent events have surely reduced the chances that Congress will ever approve the U.S.M.C.A., the Trump-negotiated replacement for Nafta.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Democrats in the House were already reluctant to pass enabling legislation, giving Trump something to boast about, unless they got some serious concessions on issues that matter to them, like labor rights. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Trump's counter was a threat to <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/12/02/us/politics/trump-withdraw-nafta.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">withdraw from Nafta</a> with no replacement. But this would have catastrophic economic effects, leading into an election year. After last week's climbdown, who believes that he would carry through on that threat?</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Trump was, of course, unhappy at news reports that accurately described his deal with Mexico over migrants as the nothingburger (nothingtaco?) it actually was. So in addition to lashing out at \"fake news,\" he introduced a <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-06-08/mexico-never-agreed-to-farm-deal-with-u-s-contradicting-trump\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">whole new claim</a>: \"MEXICO HAS AGREED TO IMMEDIATELY BEGIN BUYING LARGE QUANTITIES OF AGRICULTURAL PRODUCT FROM OUR GREAT PATRIOT FARMERS!\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">There were a few peculiar things about that claim, despite the extra persuasiveness that always comes when YOU MAKE YOUR ASSERTIONS IN CAPITAL LETTERS. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Like many Trump tweets, it reads like a clumsy translation from the original Russian (\"great patriot farmers\"?). More to the point, there was nothing at all about agriculture in the official agreement. And at the most basic level, that's just not something the Mexican government could deliver, even if it wanted to.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Some readers may recall that a few months ago China tried to avert trade conflict by promising to buy 10 million tons of U.S. <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-02-23/china-s-pledge-for-u-s-soy-buying-catches-traders-off-guard\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">soybeans</a>. The ploy didn't work, but it was at least feasible: State-owned enterprises make up a large part of the Chinese economy, and Beijing can just order them to buy stuff. Mexico, however, is a market economy, in which the private sector, not the government, decides how much Iowa corn to import.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">So was Trump confusing Mexico with China? Did he forget that the China deal he was touting months ago actually fell through? Who knows? </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">What's clear, however, is that on trade policy \u2014 his signature issue \u2014 the president of the United States is seriously out to lunch. And you might think that this would worry investors.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But as I said, markets appear to be celebrating: As I write this, stock markets are up, while long-term interest rates \u2014 a better barometer of investor views about economic prospects \u2014 are <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-06-08/donald-trump-unleashed-animal-spirits-and-then-he-crushed-them\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">off their recent lows</a>. What's going on?</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The answer, I'd suggest, is that financial markets are basically discounting Trump's rants; they've stopped treating evidence of his unfitness for office as news. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Yes, he's deeply ignorant about policy. Yes, his rage-tweets constantly remind us of his egomania and insecurity. But we've known all that for a while; Trump's personality is, in effect, already priced in.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">What investors want to know instead is the extent to which his character flaws will actually lead to destructive economic policy. Legally, Trump faces remarkably few constraints: U.S. trade law gives the president enormous discretion to impose tariffs at will, and given a spineless Senate, there are a lot of other things he can do in the name of national security. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">But as of right now, markets appear to be betting that he tweets loudly but carries a small stick.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Is this a good bet? I have my doubts. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The trade war with China still seems to be on, and Europe may be next. More generally, when you have an attention-seeking president, ignoring his antics could well provoke him into even more extreme behavior. But for now, investors are effectively treating Trump as crazy but harmless. Is America great, or what?</p><p class=\"css-jwz2nf etfikam0\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">The Times is committed to publishing </em><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/31/opinion/letters/letters-to-editor-new-york-times-women.html\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">a diversity of letters</em></a><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\"> to the editor.
