StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Almost of all of Buddy Holly's masters were lost, as were most of John Coltrane's masters in the Impulse Records collection. The fire also claimed numerous hit singles, likely including Bill Haley and His Comets' \"Rock Around the Clock,\" Etta James's \"At Last\" and the Kingsmen's \"Louie Louie.\" </p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The list of artists affected spans decades of popular music. It includes recordings by Ray Charles, B.B. King, the Four Tops, Joan Baez, Neil Diamond, Sonny and Cher, Joni Mitchell, Cat Stevens, Gladys Knight and the Pips, Al Green, Elton John, Eric Clapton, Jimmy Buffett, the Eagles, Aerosmith, Rufus and Chaka Khan, Barry White, Patti LaBelle, Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers, the Police, Sting, Steve Earle, R.E.M., Janet Jackson, Guns N' Roses, Mary J. Blige, No Doubt, Nine Inch Nails, Snoop Dogg, Nirvana, Beck, Sheryl Crow, Tupac Shakur, Eminem, 50 Cent and the Roots.</p><h2 class=\"css-ani50b eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-77cf0de2\">What are master recordings, and why do they matter?</h2><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">A master recording is the one-of-a-kind original recording of a piece of music. <!-- -->It's the source from which other vinyl records, CDs, MP3s and all other recordings are made. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">According to the article, documents show that the vault contained masters dating back decades, including multitrack recordings on which individual instruments remained isolated from one another. There were also session masters, including recordings that had never been commercially released. The recordings within the vault came from to some of the most important record labels of all time<!-- -->.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Audiophiles and audio professionals view such recordings with special regard.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"A master is the truest capture of a piece of recorded music,\" Adam Block, the former president of Legacy Recordings, Sony Music Entertainment's catalog arm, told the magazine. \"Sonically, masters can be stunning in their capturing of an event in time. Every copy thereafter is a sonic step away.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/11xp-music-coltrane/ec689f6ac5c2486f801eccd287d7c4e1-9-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:252.62222222222223px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">The John Coltrane Quartet at Rudy Van Gelder's studio in Englewood Cliffs, N.J., in 1963.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Jim Marshall</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><h2 class=\"css-ani50b eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-7d7e4ea9\">Why are we only finding about this now?</h2><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">At the time, the fire made news around the world, and the vault featured heavily in that coverage. But most articles focused only on the video recordings in the archive and, even then, news outlets largely characterized the disaster as a crisis averted.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Jody Rosen, the writer of the article, described the successful effort to play down the scope of the loss as a \"triumph of crisis management\" that involved officials working for Universal Music Group on both coasts. Those efforts were undoubtedly aimed at minimizing public embarrassment, but some suggest the company was also particularly worried about a backlash from artists and artist estates whose master recordings had been destroyed.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The real extent of the loss was laid out in litigation and company documents obtained by Mr. Rosen, a contributing writer for the magazine. </p><h2 class=\"css-ani50b eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-3ecebdd3\">How bad is the loss?</h2><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Mr. Rosen described the loss as historic, and even Universal Music Group itself \u2014 privately \u2014 viewed what happened in bleak terms: \"Lost in the fire was, undoubtedly, a huge musical heritage,\" reads one 2009 internal assessment.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Record companies have had a troubled history with such recordings and have been known to trash them in bulk. Decades ago, employees of CBS Records reportedly took power saws to multitrack masters to sell the reels as scrap metal. In the 1970s, RCA destroyed masters by Elvis Presley in a broader purge.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Because of that history, industry professionals have long questioned how committed the major music labels are to preserving what they see as priceless artifacts. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Today, most commercial recordings from the past century and beyond are controlled by only three giant record companies: Sony Music Entertainment, Warner Music Group and, of course, Universal Music Group.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-g92qtk epkadsg3\"><div class=\"css-1owp1gq epkadsg0\">Read the whole story from the magazine</div><div class=\"css-15g2oxy epkadsg2\"><div class=\"css-1cgr56x e16ij5yr6\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/11/magazine/universal-fire-master-recordings.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedLinks&amp;pgtype=Article\"><div class=\"css-i9gxme e16ij5yr4\"><div class=\"css-b4q99a e16ij5yr2\">The Day the Music Burned</div><div class=\"css-u59xwy e16ij5yr3\">It was the biggest disaster in the history of the music business \u2014 and almost nobody knew. This is the story of the 2008 Universal fire.</div><time class=\"css-rqb9bm e16638kd0\" datetime=\"2019-06-11\">June 11, 2019</time></div><div class=\"css-wexrmg e16ij5yr0\"><img class=\"css-1g9kf2h e16ij5yr1\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Universal-image11/16mag-Universal-image11-threeByTwoSmallAt2X-v6.jpg\"/></div></a></div></div></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/11/us/master-recordings-universal-fire.html", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">Recordings by Elton John, Nirvana and Thousands More Lost in Fire - The New York Times</title>"}, "state-legislatures-partisan-polarized": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">When J.B. Pritzker took over as the governor of Illinois this year, Democratic lawmakers, who had spent four years at an impasse with his Republican predecessor, vowed that their party's new grip on the State Capitol would bring immediate change.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The pace has been startling. In recent months, Illinois legislators have moved sharply to the left, deeming abortion a <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://www.ilga.gov/legislation/101/SB/10100SB0025ham001.htm\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">fundamental right</a> for women no matter what the Supreme Court might decide, raising the minimum wage, taking steps to legalize recreational marijuana and introducing a graduated income tax.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Some 700 miles to the south, the Alabama State Capitol, dominated by Republicans, has raced in the opposite direction.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Alabama lawmakers voted during this term to <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/14/us/abortion-law-alabama.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">ban most abortions</a>. They <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://legiscan.com/AL/bill/SB69/2019\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">eliminated marriage licenses</a>, so that probate judges opposed to same-sex marriage would not have to sign marriage certificates. And they approved requiring sex offenders who commit crimes involving children to undergo <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://legiscan.com/AL/bill/HB379/2019\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">chemical castration</a> at their own expense.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Gov. Kay Ivey of Alabama, a fellow Republican, earlier signed the abortion and marriage license bills, and on Monday her office announced that she had signed the castration legislation.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">It is the first time in more than a century that all but one state legislature is dominated by a single party. Most legislative sessions have ended or are scheduled to end in a matter of days in capitals across the nation, and Republican-held states have rushed forward with conservative agendas as those controlled by Democrats have pushed through liberal ones.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Any hope that single-party control in the states might ease the tone of political discourse has not borne out. Lopsided party dominance has not brought resignation; instead of minority parties conceding that they lack the numbers to effectively fight back, the mood has grown more tense and vitriolic.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"The whole nation is speaking about how divisive we are,\" Thomas Jackson, a Democrat in the Alabama House of Representatives, told colleagues during a contentious meeting last month.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/us/11statefights2/ce2472fbaf8c428d87a48f0e40ca7447-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><img alt=\"\" class=\"css-1m50asq\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/us/11statefights2/ce2472fbaf8c428d87a48f0e40ca7447-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" itemprop=\"url\" sizes=\"((min-width: 600px) and (max-width: 1004px)) 84vw, (min-width: 1005px) 60vw, 100vw\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/us/11statefights2/ce2472fbaf8c428d87a48f0e40ca7447-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" srcset=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/us/11statefights2/ce2472fbaf8c428d87a48f0e40ca7447-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/us/11statefights2/ce2472fbaf8c428d87a48f0e40ca7447-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/us/11statefights2/ce2472fbaf8c428d87a48f0e40ca7447-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w\"/></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">A group including three Democratic senators stood among the empty desks of Republican senators at the Oregon State Capitol in May.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Connor Radnovich/Statesman-Journal via Associated Press</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In Oregon, where Democrats control state government, Republicans <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.opb.org/news/article/oregon-republican-senate-shutdown-education-funding-vote/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">boycotted </a>sessions for several days over disagreements about taxes and gun control. In Tennessee, where Republicans are in charge, Democrats staged a walkout during a heated and chaotic budget debate, and Republicans <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.tennessean.com/story/news/politics/2019/05/02/tennessee-general-assembly-final-days-111-th-legislative-session-house-senate-republicans-democrats/3615928002/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">ordered the police</a> to go find them.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In New York, the State Legislature passed several laws that had been blocked in previous years by Republicans, who lost control of the Senate earlier this year after a decade in power. Those measures included a law <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/28/nyregion/child-sex-abuse-victims.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">extending the period of time</a> for victims of childhood sexual abuse to file lawsuits, and several others <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/29/nyregion/gun-laws-new-york.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">restricting the use of firearms</a>, including bans on bump stocks and teachers carrying guns in schools.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">And in Colorado, where Democrats dominate in the capital, Republicans were so upset about the stream of new laws being passed that they demanded each bill be read aloud to slow the pace. Democrats responded by having five computers <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://twitter.com/samuelbrasch/status/1105211490938716160/video/1\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">simultaneously \"read\" bills</a>. The computers were able to whip through hundreds of pages in minutes, but the result was <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QCpq_3jlP30&amp;feature=youtu.be\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">gibberish</a>.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-cfo9c3\"></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Colorado Republicans promptly sued. They won in court, but Democrats went on \u2014 at a moderated pace \u2014 to pass legislation that many Republicans opposed, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://leg.colorado.gov/bills/hb18-1274\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">reducing greenhouse gas emissions</a>, banning <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/01/us/gay-conversion-therapy-colorado.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">gay conversion therapy</a> for minors and creating a <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://leg.colorado.gov/sites/default/files/documents/2019A/bills/2019a_1168_ren.pdf\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">reinsurance program</a> to lower health care costs.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">This year was always <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/28/us/democrats-gun-control-healthcare.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">poised to be contentious</a> in statehouses. Across the nation, nearly 1,700 new lawmakers won seats in last fall's elections. The vast majority of the newcomers were Democrats, who won control of six new legislative chambers, meaning that they now dominate both chambers in 18 states. But Republicans continue to control the majority of state legislatures, with 29.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Analysts said that issues addressed by state legislatures this year, which included <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.leg.state.nv.us/App/NELIS/REL/80th2019/Bill/6174/Overview\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">gun control</a>, health care, education and <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://leginfo.legislature.ca.gov/faces/billNavClient.xhtml?bill_id=201920200AB392\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">police procedures</a>, might have more immediate, lasting effect than anything approved in Washington, D.C., where government is divided.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The roots of the polarization in state legislatures can be traced to <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://ballotpedia.org/State_legislative_elections,_2010\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">elections in 2010</a>, when Republicans made decisive gains in statehouses and pressed for policies that included restricting labor unions and abortion access, while expanding gun rights, according to Sarah F. Anzia, a political scientist at the University of California, Berkeley.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Around the same time, Dr. Anzia said, national organizations representing interest groups ranging from <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.aft.org/action/election-2018\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">teachers</a> to gun owners became more active in state capitals, because they found it far easier to make headway in places like <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nraila.org/legal-legislation/state-legislation/california/2019/february-2019-litigation-report/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Sacramento</a> and <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.wvea.org/content/tax-reform-committee-updated-june-15-0\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Charleston, W.Va., </a>than in Washington because of gridlock in Congress.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The number of states with either supermajorities of Democrats that also have Democratic governors (California, Nevada and Oregon, among others) or Republicans with Republican governors (Alabama, Ohio and Tennessee, among others) has grown, too, meaning that many lawmakers rarely feel the need to compromise.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"If you are a Republican in one state, you are probably going to be pushing the same agenda as a Republican in another state, and the same is true for Democrats,\" said Dr. Anzia. \"That hasn't always been true, and the result is that now more than ever, state legislatures are key players in these partisan battles over politics.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In Minnesota, the <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/28/us/democrats-gun-control-healthcare.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">only state </a>left with a divided legislature, promises of bipartisanship sometimes devolved into stalemate.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">During a budget standoff last month, Tim Walz, the Democratic governor who campaigned last year on a pledge to work across the aisle, angrily denounced Republicans for blocking gun control efforts and supporting deep tax cuts, saying those policies \"fit better in Mississippi and Alabama than they do in Minnesota.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Ultimately, Democrats could win neither new gun laws nor new tax increases, and Republicans also failed to win approval for the bulk of their agenda.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Still, once the session ended last month, Governor Walz said that \"Minnesota is showing the rest of the nation that Republicans and Democrats can still find compromise and work together to get things done,\" citing spending increases for public education and efforts to fight opioid addiction.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Alabama and Illinois \u2014 one overwhelmingly red, the other blue \u2014 were more representative of this year's tone, providing perhaps the best examples of political parties moving to enact utterly different agendas.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/us/11statefights/89bbd3e6b3b3469a8e35ab8ff5dae9e3-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:279.0444444444444px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Illinois Governor J.B. Pritzker cheered as Illinois Senate President John Cullerton, a fellow Democrat, made final remarks after a frenetic spring in Springfield, Ill.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Justin L. Fowler/The State Journal-Register via Associated Press</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">After Alabama <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/14/us/abortion-law-alabama.html?module=inline\" title=\"\"> effectively banned abortion</a> last month, female lawmakers in Illinois responded almost immediately, pressing through a bill expanding abortion rights in their state. (Abortion rights groups have sued to stop the Alabama law from taking effect.) And while Illinois voted to <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"http://www.ilga.gov/legislation/BillStatus.asp?DocTypeID=SB&amp;DocNum=3432&amp;GAID=14&amp;SessionID=91&amp;LegID=111418\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">allow sports betting</a> and to legalize recreational marijuana, Alabama failed to approve either a <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://legiscan.com/AL/bill/SB220/2019\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">state lottery</a> or medical marijuana.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">It was Alabama's abortion measure, the strictest in the nation, that sparked the most contentious debate of any legislation this session.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">During debates in the Legislature, Rolanda Hollis, a Democratic member of the House of Representatives, read a poem to colleagues called <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/national/archive/2013/07/if-my-vagina-was-gun-revives-tradition-protest-poetry/313217/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">\"If My Vagina Was a Gun\"</a> that she said illustrated Alabama's consistent protection of Second Amendment rights but not abortion rights.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Bobby Singleton, a Senate Democrat, told his Republican colleagues that they had \"aborted\" and \"raped\" Alabama by supporting the legislation, which was approved generally along party lines.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Terry Lathan, the chair of the Alabama Republican Party, downplayed the uproar over the abortion bill, saying she had seen worse \u2014 including when a Republican senator <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=knXgcd_iAUg\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">punched</a> a Democratic colleague on the Senate floor in 2007.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"This is the political arena,\" she said. \"Everyone needs to put on their big girl and boy pants. I mean, come on!\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In Illinois, Republicans were in much the same position as Democrats in Alabama: Outnumbered and outflanked. And like Alabama Democrats, Illinois Republicans lost nearly every vote of significance.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In addition to voting to raise the minimum wage to $15 by 2025, the state legislature became the first in the nation to pass a bill legalizing both the sale and possession of marijuana. (In other states, voters have approved such laws through ballot initiatives.)</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Dale Righter, a Republican in the Illinois Senate, said that without power, Republicans' hopes relied on conservative Democratic voters deciding that their lawmakers had gone too far.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"I have no doubt that there are Democratic voters saying, 'Hey, this isn't what I signed up for,'\" he said.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/11/us/state-legislatures-partisan-polarized.html#commentsContainer", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">With Most States Under One Party\u2019s Control, America Grows More Divided - The New York Times</title>"}, "womens-soccer-inequality-pay": {"body": "<section class=\"meteredContent css-1i2y565\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" name=\"articleBody\"><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In spring 2018, Abby Wambach, the most decorated soccer player in American history, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wJe40l2waxs\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">gave a commencement address</a> at Barnard College that went viral. The player who had scored more goals than any other, male or female, in international competition described standing onstage at the ESPYs the year after she retired in 2015, receiving the Icon Award alongside two peers, Peyton Manning and Kobe Bryant. \"I felt so grateful,\" she recalled. \"I had a momentary feeling of having arrived; like, we women had finally made it.\" As the athletes exited the stage, each having, as Wambach put it, \"left it all on the field for decades with the same ferocity, talent and commitment,\" it occurred to her that while the sacrifices the men made for their careers were nearly identical to her own, their new lives would not resemble hers in one fundamental way. \"Kobe and Peyton walked away from their careers with something I didn't have: enormous bank accounts,\" Wambach said. \"Because of that, they had something else I didn't have: freedom. Their hustling days were over; mine were just beginning.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The United States women's national team is the best in the world and has been for decades. Since the FIFA Women's World Cup was inaugurated in 1991, the United States has won three of the seven titles, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2015/07/06/sports/soccer/womens-world-cup-usa-defeats-japan-to-win-title.html?searchResultPosition=4&amp;module=inline\" title=\"\">including the most recent one in 2015</a>. Since women's soccer became an Olympic sport in 1996, it has won four of six gold medals. The team has been ranked No.1 by FIFA for 10 of the last 11 years and has produced some of the biggest female sports stars of the last several decades, from Mia Hamm to Wambach to the current starting center forward, Alex Morgan. The squad playing at the World Cup this month in France includes Morgan; her accomplice on the left wing, the Tilda Swinton doppelg\\xe4nger Megan Rapinoe; and the previous World Cup's hat-trick-scoring hero, Carli Lloyd; along with newcomers like the elegant but deadly Mallory Pugh and the ingenious, bruising midfielder Lindsey Horan. The American team is favored to successfully defend its title, despite a field of opponents whose depth, fitness and all-around sophistication improved drastically even in the past four years, reflecting the rapid growth of women's soccer globally. \"This is the first World Cup where I feel like \u2014 and I'm rejoicing over this \u2014 I can count potential World Cup winners on more than one hand,\" the former player and current ESPN commentator Julie Foudy said when calling a recent match between the United States and Mexico.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-03/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-1-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><img alt=\"\" class=\"css-1m50asq\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-03/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-1-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" itemprop=\"url\" sizes=\"((min-width: 600px) and (max-width: 1004px)) 84vw, (min-width: 1005px) 60vw, 100vw\" src=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-03/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-1-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale\" srcset=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-03/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-1-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-03/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-1-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-03/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-1-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w\"/></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-i48y28 e13ogyst0\">Young fans at the exhibition game between the United States and Belgium on April 7.</span><span class=\"css-nt1l96 e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Dina Litovsky/Redux, for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">It was particularly important, then, in the months leading up to this moment, for the American women to keep their focus, minimize distractions and avoid drama at all costs. Which they did, with one enormous exception. On March 8, they <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/03/08/sports/womens-soccer-team-lawsuit-gender-discrimination.html?searchResultPosition=1&amp;module=inline\" title=\"\">sued the United States Soccer Federation</a>, claiming \"purposeful gender discrimination.\" \"The bottom line is simple,\" the star defender Becky Sauerbrunn said in a statement. \"It is wrong for us to be paid and valued less for our work because of our gender.\" Rapinoe, also in a statement, mentioned the responsibility the team feels to advocate \"on behalf of our teammates, future teammates, fellow women athletes and women all around the world.\" This was 95 days before the team's first World Cup match in France and mere weeks before the beginning of its next training camp \u2014 a weeklong blend of intense practice and tryouts aimed at enabling Coach Jill Ellis and her staff to get the alchemy just right. But the players felt they could not wait. \"We don't always want to be patient,\" Morgan tells me. \"You have to seize the moment.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2015/06/05/magazine/why-is-us-womens-soccer-still-fighting-to-exist.html?module=inline\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2015/06/05/magazine/why-is-us-womens-soccer-still-fighting-to-exist.html\" title=\"\">[Why is U.S. women's soccer still fighting to exist?]</a></a></p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The lawsuit's timing may be dramatic, but it was the natural next step in a continuing dispute that centers on equal compensation. Members of the U.S.W.N.T. have been pursuing fair compensation for years, with only marginal improvement: The lawsuit asserts, for example, that from 2013 to 2016, if a male and a female national team player each played 20 exhibition games in a year, members of the men's squad would have earned an average of $263,320, while members of the women's squad would have earned a maximum of $99,000. The suit also claims that \"during the period relevant to this case,\" the women's team earned more for U.S. Soccer than the men's team did. It cites numbers from the 2016 fiscal year that indicate that the federation had expected a combined net loss for the national teams of $429,929, but that largely because of the women's team's successes it revised its projections to a $17.7 million profit.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-04/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-5-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.1333333333334px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-i48y28 e13ogyst0\">Christen Press during a game against South Africa at Levi's Stadium in Santa Clara, Calif.</span><span class=\"css-nt1l96 e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Dina Litovsky/Redux, for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In a response filed on May 7, U.S. Soccer denies many of the specifics provided in the lawsuit, including those mentioned above, but it doesn't dispute that the men's and women's players are not paid equally. Instead, it asserts that those inequities are a result of \"different pay structures for performing different work.\" It characterizes as \"misleading and inaccurate\" the claims that the women's team generates more revenue than the men's, while also framing the women's and men's teams as so different from each other that they can't legitimately be compared at all. This is true in at least one sense: The women are way, way better. The men's national team lost in the round of 16 at the 2014 World Cup and didn't even qualify for the 2018 World Cup. American men haven't won an Olympic medal in more than a century. Partly as a consequence of their superior results, from 2015 to 2018, the women's team played 19 more matches than the men. In other words, the women aren't working as hard as their male counterparts for less money; they're working <em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">harder</em> for less money. For the record, the men's team's players association released a statement of full-throated support for their women's team compatriots and the mutual goal of equal pay.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In her Barnard speech, Wambach said she regretted being so caught up in gratitude for what she and her peers did receive that she \"missed opportunities to demand equality for all of us.\" Her former teammates do not intend to make that same mistake. They are better paid than any women's sports team in history, and at least as well known, but it's not enough. Not only because by the players' calculations they are making as little as 38 cents to their male counterparts' dollar, but because these players feel a responsibility to fight, in public, on the biggest stage possible, while they can. \"It's wonderful to be a professional athlete and feel fulfilled, but at the same time, what sort of legacy do you want to leave?\" Morgan wonders. \"I had this dream of being a professional soccer player, and I never knew it entailed being a role model, being an inspiration, standing up for things I believe in, standing up for gender equality. But now I don't know a world where I just play soccer. It goes hand in hand.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-05/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-6-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.1333333333334px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-i48y28 e13ogyst0\">Megan Rapinoe on the ground during a game against South Africa on May 12.</span><span class=\"css-nt1l96 e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Dina Litovsky/Redux, for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">On a glittering April</strong> evening in Los Angeles, 20,941 fans crowded into the Banc of California Stadium, home to Major League Soccer's Los Angeles F.C., to watch the American women trounce the 20th-ranked Belgians, 6-0, in a match of no real consequence. (This was one of several exhibition matches, known as \"friendlies,\" the women's team played before leaving for France.) Three teenage girls gathered on the south end of the stadium near the Belgian goal. Two wanted to head up to the mezzanine to see if they could get a glimpse of the Hollywood celebrities in the house \u2014 Natalie Portman, Jessica Chastain, Jennifer Garner, Eva Longoria and Uzo Aduba were all in the V.I.P. box, hanging out with Megan Rapinoe, who was not playing because of a mild injury. But one of the teenagers, a tall brunette in jean shorts and a cropped T-shirt, wasn't ready to go actress hunting yet. She stood staring at the action on the pitch, mesmerized. \"Let me just see this last play,\" she pleaded \u2014 and right then, Carli Lloyd cut back behind her defender and threaded a perfect pass to Alex Morgan, who chipped it into the back of the net.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The official Time's Up Instagram account later posted a photo of the actresses, all Time's Up supporters, in their U.S.W.N.T. jerseys, with the caption \"It's time for U.S. Soccer Federation to pay their women players what they deserve.\" That Time's Up is choosing to formally align itself, and its quest for equal pay in Hollywood, with the women's national team is particularly gratifying for the players. They consider their fight to be in keeping with the larger social-justice stories of this era, from the rise of explicitly feminist movements like Time's Up and #MeToo to Black Lives Matter and L.G.B.T. advocacy. \"It's one and the same,\" Rapinoe says. \"I get asked this question a lot, like, 'Where does this come from?' or 'Why do you stand up for these things?' To me, it's literally all the same, insofar as I want people to respect who I am, what I am \u2014 being gay, being a woman, being a professional athlete, whatever. That is the exact same thing as what Colin did.\" Rapinoe began kneeling during the national anthem in solidarity with Colin Kaepernick in September 2016; in March 2017, U.S. Soccer instituted a policy requiring players to \"stand respectfully.\" (Rapinoe now stands but does not place her hand over her heart.) \"Who do you want to be?\" Rapinoe says. \"What kind of person do you want to be for yourself, but also in the larger context of the country and in the world?\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-06/16mag-Soccer-image-06-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:320.2888888888889px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-i48y28 e13ogyst0\">Carli Lloyd, Alex Morgan and Megan Rapinoe.</span><span class=\"css-nt1l96 e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Dina Litovsky/Redux, for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Serena Williams, asked by reporters to comment on the women's soccer team's lawsuit after a second-round victory at the BNP Paribas Open in Indian Wells, Calif., called the pay discrepancy \"ludicrous,\" adding, \"I think at some point, in every sport, you have to have those pioneers, and maybe it's the time for soccer.\" Indeed, American women's soccer has its original class of pioneers: the so-called 99ers, members of the 1999 World Cup-winning team. At the Los Angeles friendly, Jennifer Garner wore one of their names \u2014 Mia Hamm \u2014 on her jersey, Aduba wore the legendary goalkeeper Briana Scurry's number and Jessica Chastain wore the jersey of a player with whom she happens to share a surname: Brandi Chastain. It was Brandi Chastain who became a kind of aesthetic allegory for the spirit of the national team when, after sinking the winning penalty against China in the 1999 final, she whipped off her jersey in celebration. The image of Chastain in her sports bra, six-pack on display, triumph on her face, is one of the most famous in the history of sports, both because it captured a huge moment in soccer and because it launched a backlash against Chastain, who was accused of being disrespectful by critics who appeared to believe it was cool for male players to celebrate in this way but uncouth for women to do the same.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/24/sports/womens-world-cup-jamaica.html?module=inline\" title=\"\"><em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">[Read about the Women's World Cup's other inequality: rich vs. poor.]</em></a></p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Many of the 99ers were in attendance at the friendly to celebrate the 20th anniversary of their World Cup victory. It was that win that established the Americans as women's soccer's first true global stars, the first group of players with the clout to move the needle on issues big (better pay) and small (getting uniforms in women's sizes). Before that World Cup, which was held for the first time in the United States, the team was accustomed to playing to crowds of 5,000, but the 1999 World Cup final at the Rose Bowl drew 90,185 people, still the record for a women's sporting event. After they won, the players toured the country like rock stars, visiting the White House, Disneyland and \"The Late Show,\" where David Letterman referred to them as \"babe city.\" When the dust settled, however, America's newest sweethearts discovered that they were out of work. There was still no viable professional league in the United States.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The 99ers were determined to use the leverage gained by their victory to start a fully professional league, the W.U.S.A. But by the time the national team (including a young Abby Wambach) was defending its title four years later, the league had already folded. And so it went for the next decade. The women's national team continued to be among the most elite in the world, but it returned home after major victories (Olympic gold in 2004, 2008, 2012) to a succession of professional leagues that never stabilized, all the while clawing out incremental financial advances in a series of collective-bargaining agreements with U.S. Soccer.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image07/6e1cda8924374b4988f1edcbdcf5010d-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-i48y28 e13ogyst0\">Members of the United States women's national team.</span><span class=\"css-nt1l96 e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Dina Litovsky/Redux, for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The National Women's Soccer League, now in its seventh season, is the longest-running professional women's soccer league ever in the United States, but its players still do not make a living wage: The minimum salary was just bumped up to $16,538. Major League Soccer pays male players a minimum salary in the $50,000-a-year range.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The women's national team's lawsuit will play out in a Los Angeles courtroom on a date yet to be set by the Federal District Court, where U.S. Soccer will need to show that the pay disparities between their two teams exist for some reason, any reason, other than sex. According to the women's lawsuit, U.S. Soccer has said it can't grant economic parity because \"market realities are such that the women do not deserve to be paid equally to the men.\" Then there's the \"But you agreed to be paid less\" argument, which appears to be central to U.S. Soccer's strategy: In April 2017, the women's national team and U.S. Soccer signed a new collective-bargaining agreement in which the women gained ground but did not receive the equal pay they were hoping for. \"It was the best deal we could get at the time,\" Rapinoe says.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The previous agreement had been in place since 2013. As the 2016 Olympics loomed, the female players were reportedly considering striking \u2014 hoping to leverage their position as defending gold medalists to increase their shot at earning equal compensation in their next collective-bargaining agreement \u2014 when U.S. Soccer sued to prevent them from doing so and won.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-i67pzw e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/16/magazine/16mag-Soccer-image-02/6410c820c1284b91b830fb31dde2daf7-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:541.3333333333334px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-i48y28 e13ogyst0\">Alex Morgan (left) and Megan Rapinoe (right) celebrating with Tobin Heath after her goal against Mexico on May 26.</span><span class=\"css-nt1l96 e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Dina Litovsky/Redux, for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Shortly before that ruling came down, five members of the team \u2014 Megan Rapinoe, Carli Lloyd, Becky Sauerbrunn, Alex Morgan and Hope Solo, the goalkeeper at the time \u2014 filed a federal discrimination complaint with the Equal Employment Opportunity Commission, which is required before you can sue. This February, when the team was between training camps, the five original players named in the 2016 complaint finally received a response in the form of \"right to sue\" letters, meaning that no determination had been reached one way or another and that they had 90 days to file suit in federal court. So they did.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The 2019 Women's World Cup is expected to be the most watched in history. In the United States, these matches will most likely be among the highest-rated soccer games ever played. (The 2015 final in Canada, between the United States and Japan, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2015/07/07/sports/soccer/womens-world-cup-final-was-most-watched-soccer-game-in-united-states-history.html?searchResultPosition=6&amp;module=inline\" title=\"\">averaged 23 million English-language viewers</a> in the States, six million more than the 2014 Men's World Cup final.) Yes, the Americans are favored, but no team in the history of the Women's World Cup has ever won back-to-back titles, and the United States has lately shown some vulnerability. The last major tournament it won was the 2015 World Cup. In 2017, it failed to perform as well as expected in two invitational events hosted on home soil, coming in last in the SheBelieves Cup and finishing second to Australia in the Tournament of Nations. At that point, several senior players, in what Sports Illustrated called a \"player revolt,\" initiated conversations with U.S. Soccer about replacing Coach Jill Ellis.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">This unrest came in the wake of the most psychologically gutting performance in team history, at the 2016 Olympics in Brazil. For the first time ever, the team failed to make the Olympic gold medal match; they lost on penalty kicks to Sweden in the quarterfinals. To say the humiliation of this defeat still stings is to put it mildly. \"A lot of the players on this team that have never been to a World Cup did go to the Olympics and were a part of the team that didn't perform as well as we should have and had the worst exit that we've ever had in the Olympics, and we never want to replicate that ever in this program, but especially this World Cup,\" Alex Morgan told me in an unusually breathless burst. \"That's definitely in the back of my mind.\" At the end of 2017, U.S. Soccer made it clear that Ellis was staying, and by 2018 things had stabilized a bit; the team went undefeated last year. But in their first match of 2019, they lost 3-1 to France, a rising power that will no doubt be emboldened this summer, playing on its home turf.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In filing suit when they did, the players set themselves up for a very tense few months \u2014 in part because they believe that their performance on the pitch holds the key to their progress off it. \"Always and forever, how well the team does on the biggest stage is probably the most important thing,\" Rapinoe says. \"That's what I stress to these kids,\" she continues, referring to the younger players like Pugh and Horan, who walked into the national team's world believing that their job was merely to play the best soccer of their lives and are now learning that's only part of it. \"Everything is more and better,\" Rapinoe says. \"I want them to understand that it's better because we earned it; but it's also better because we won. The most important thing is continuing to win.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1l6nq8w\" style=\"margin:0 auto\"><div class=\"medium css-17dprlf\" data-id=\"100000006546471\" data-slug=\"16mag-soccer-pullquote1\" style=\"max-width:600px\"><iframe class=\"css-sqdgy8\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\" src=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/admin/100000006546471.embedded.html?\" width=\"100%\"></iframe></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">In the lobby</strong> of a boutique hotel in downtown Santa Barbara, where the national team stayed during its World Cup training camp in March, well-heeled tourists poured cucumber water from glass vats and discussed where to lunch. The whole place smelled like expensive candles. \"No more Marriott Residence Inn for us,\" Rapinoe said with a grin after settling into an overstuffed love seat next to a stunning bouquet of flowers.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">About an hour earlier, the 28 athletes who were in contention for the World Cup team (23 would make the cut) finished practice. As some traipsed through the lobby, sweaty and joking with one another, a few sang the chorus to Lil Nas X's \"Old Town Road\" (\"Can't nobody tell me nothin'/You can't tell me nothin'\\u2009\"), which had been a fixture in camp. Soon they would shower and have group lunch. The day before, the players also had morning training followed by lunch, then a meeting with the team's sports psychologist before group dinner. After training, there are ice baths and other recovery work. This is how the players' lives are programmed: Eat, train, recover, eat, sleep, repeat. \"Soccer is like 'Groundhog Day,'\\u2009\" Rapinoe says. \"It's great, it's fine, but it's not that exciting all the time.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"We know the sacrifices we make; it's no different than what men make,\" Carli Lloyd says. \"We're away from our families. We're away from our friends. We're spending every waking hour dedicating ourselves to this.\" If an international squad is a collection of roles filled by a rotating cast of actual human beings, Lloyd is currently in the \"seasoned veteran in the twilight of her career\" spot, the one Wambach was in during the last World Cup. A two-time FIFA player of the year, Lloyd scored a hat trick in the first 16 minutes of the 2015 final against Japan, topping off an already remarkable run of play. Lloyd is 36 now. She feels as sharp as ever, she says, and has been playing largely as a second-half substitute in these recent friendlies, scoring thrilling clutch goals. But she is not likely to get a ton of playing time in France, and even if she does, this is almost certainly her last World Cup.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">When I joked about how it would be amusing to try to train with her, she snickered and told me about one reporter who tried that and tore her A.C.L. \u2014 \"You could hear the pop\" \u2014 and another who broke her wrist trying to block a Lloyd shot. But Lloyd turned wistful when she shared that she and her husband are planning to start a family in the next few years, but in looking at their bank account she realized: \"I can't just say, 'O.K., this is my last game, and I've made tens of millions of dollars and it's stashed away and we're good.'\\u2009\" For the moment, Lloyd has no interest in retiring. She remains committed to the lawsuit \u2014 though she acknowledges she \"may be done playing by the time this gets resolved\" \u2014 and to winning in France. She also deeply enjoys the rigorous two-a-day training sessions she does when home in New Jersey. This is all part of what Lloyd calls her eternal addiction to \"chasing something I need to improve on.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">They all talk like this, about a state of permanent dissatisfaction and a pleasure taken in pursuing the very perfection they know is unattainable. The one thing every of them has is this superhuman drive. \"Players come in all the time, great players, sometimes more talented players,\" says the forward Christen Press, the squad's resident \"What does it all mean?\" existential philosopher, who first played on the team in 2012. \"The players that survive here are the most competitive ones. No one on this team has been here for more than two years and not felt like they had their face planted on the ground. Many just don't get up. The people that last here get up.\" She continues: \"It's such a small, elite group that you're filtered out if you don't have that.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">If Lloyd represents one role in the life cycle of a national team player, Lindsey Horan represents its opposite: the young-gun rising star and one of the picks to emerge from this World Cup a newly minted superstar. Her path is itself a testament to the progress that has been made in opportunities for American women who love to play soccer. When Lloyd made her debut on the team in 2005, there was <em class=\"css-2fg4z9 e1gzwzxm0\">still</em> no viable professional league in the United States. Lloyd played all four years at Rutgers, then came to the national team \"right when they were negotiating stable salaries and contracts,\" she remembers. Horan, on the other hand, went straight to the pros from high school. This is a controversial move. Press calls it \"crazy\" for most players, laughing and shaking her head. \"The league is not stable enough,\" she explains. \"If you're playing in the N.B.A., you can make two years of your salary and pay for your college anytime you want to go back. But that's not the case with the N.W.S.L.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Advisable or not, by 2012, when Horan got on the plane to France to begin her time at Paris Saint-Germain, professional women's leagues were prominent enough, in the States and in Europe, that such a move was possible. It was her dream, so she went for it. Horan is not much for keeping her cards close to her chest. Getting called up, training, playing well in international tournaments, then focusing on showing her best game in camp these last months has been enough of a challenge, she says, without the added pressure to become a civil rights activist overnight. \"It has been very hard,\" Horan says. \"I've always just been like: Oh, I love soccer. I love being here. I'm so happy to be a part of this team.\" But lately, that has shifted. \"I've always wanted to just stay out of that and focus on the game, but now I think that is almost selfish, because we do have a voice, and so many people watch us, and we're their inspirations, and we're their idols, and us speaking up is huge.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The \"four or five girls that are very vocal\" who Horan says helped her reach this conclusion \u2014 the team leaders when it comes to advocacy \u2014 have a knack for instilling a sense of social responsibility in others. \"We try, first of all, education,\" Rapinoe says. \"We break down the inequities. We tell them: This is why we are choosing to take this stance, for these reasons. We try to show specifically how it affects each individual player, but then also the team as a whole.\" Could someone have declined to join the lawsuit if she wanted to? \"Yeah,\" says Rapinoe, slowly. \"It's always possible, and we had some players that took longer.\" But, she says, \"If you want the door open, you have to open it.\"</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\"><strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\">On a welcome</strong> bright April day after a very wet stretch in Denver, 10-year-old Lilli and her 9-year-old friend, Reese, sat in their soccer kits, legs dangling off white folding chairs, in front of City Hall. This was a school day, but Reese's mother brought them to watch two of their heroes, Lindsey Horan and Mallory Pugh, receive an honorary street sign and a \"challenge coin,\" the equivalent of a key to the city. Pugh and Horan are both Denver-area natives, and both came up through the hypercompetitive ranks of Colorado youth soccer. They are models for what Lilli and Reese plan to become when they grow up: pro soccer players. \"It's educational!\" Lilli insisted of this field trip for two. Then she showed off the ball, shoes, shin guards and backpack she had brought to have signed. By which player? \"Both of them!\" Lilli plays offense, and this kind of game-day aggressiveness will come in handy for her on the field, for sure, but it may be even more important off the field if she's serious about a career in professional soccer.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Watching Horan and Pugh stand only somewhat awkwardly next to the mayor, with their parents snapping pictures and a local news crew on hand to document the quaint pageantry, felt like watching the opening scene in a biopic. Each is already a groundbreaker: Pugh is the youngest American player, at 17, ever to play in an Olympic-qualifying match, and Horan is the first American woman to go straight from high school to the pros. They now play for top teams in the N.W.S.L. \u2014 Pugh for the Washington Spirit, Horan for the Portland Thorns \u2014 and they have high-profile endorsement deals (Pugh with Nike, Horan with Adidas). Pugh and Horan didn't know this yet, but they would each make the World Cup squad \u2014 another milestone reached. But the question remains: Will one or both of these players break the record so many of her predecessors could not and become the first in women's soccer history to retire without having to worry about her next paycheck? And if not Pugh or Horan, how about by the time we get to Lilli or Reese?</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The 28 women suing U.S. Soccer have, in some cases, very little in common other than their sport. Avowed Christians and atheists, gay and straight, politically active and not, they have nonetheless rallied behind this collective cause. \"You really do need everyone,\" Rapinoe says. \"It's a crazy intimate environment. We're not all really, really close, but we're extremely intimate.\" At the hotel in Santa Barbara, she brought up the concept of \"the double earn,\" a reference to the unpaid labor taken on by women, especially at home, that goes largely unacknowledged; Rapinoe was drawing a parallel between that work and the work that she and her teammates are having to do to secure equal rights that should already be theirs. The soccer players, differences aside, have something powerful in common besides competitive drive: They are, every one of them, from 20-year-old defender Tierna Davidson to 36-year-old Carli Lloyd, pulling a double shift. \"We really don't want to be doing all of this all of the time,\" Rapinoe says. \"We'd much prefer to not be engaging in litigations. We'd much prefer not to have to be the nag in the room. We'd prefer to be thought partners and business partners.\" Rapinoe sat up a little straighter in her seat. \"But obviously that's not the case.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div></section>", "link": "/2019/06/10/magazine/womens-soccer-inequality-pay.html#commentsContainer", "title": "<title data-rh=\"true\">The Best Women\u2019s Soccer Team class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">On her two YouTube channels, Bethany Gaskin chats up her audience while downing huge meals, often seafood, like king crab.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Maddie McGarvey for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">CINCINNATI \u2014 Most of us can probably agree that eating food is more enjoyable than watching someone else eat food. For one, it's a basic human need. It also tastes good a lot of the time. Not to mention, people can be pretty gross when they eat, especially when they do so in over-the-top, finger-licking fashion.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Still, hundreds of thousands of people tune in each week to watch Bethany Gaskin binge-eat shellfish on YouTube.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Mrs.<!-- --> Gaskin, 44, has capitalized on the popularity of a food-video genre known as mukbang, which involves scarfing down, on camera, more grub than should rightly be consumed in a single sitting. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">On her two YouTube channels, <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCG_Nlvx1EoxkeZkuLjelWdA\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">Bloveslife</a> and <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCqzQA4tjCh-uAOAHz8_qGpQ\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">BlovesASMR Eating Her Way</a>, Mrs. Gaskin chats up her audience while eating king crab legs, mussels, lobster tails, hard-boiled eggs and roasted red potatoes. The videos, produced in her Cincinnati home, have made her a millionaire, she said. But getting into the business wasn't about money; mukbang was more of a calling than a vocation.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">\"I think of mukbanging as a ministry,\" Mrs. Gaskin said. \"I didn't consult with my husband before I quit my job. I knew this was it, and I quit by faith.\"</p><h2 class=\"css-edk2dh eoo0vm40\" id=\"link-6dd489f0\">The Spread of Binge Culture</h2><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Mukbang seems to have begun as an internet trend more than a decade ago in South Korea.<!-- --> The name is a mash-up of the Korean words for <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/magazine-31130947\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">let's eat (\"muk-ja\") and broadcasting (\"bang-song\")</a>. Korean live-streamers often schedule their mukbang videos to align with <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://qz.com/592710/why-some-koreans-make-10000-a-month-to-eat-on-camera/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\">dinnertime hours</a>, so their viewers eating alone at home feel like they're sharing a meal with a friend.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Viewers cite other benefits too. Watching the videos can serve as an appetite-curbing exercise. And for a certain subset, the sounds of a person eating foster an <a class=\"css-1g7m0tk\" href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/04/04/magazine/how-asmr-videos-became-a-sensation-youtube.html?module=inline\" title=\"\">autonomous sensory meridian response, or A.S.M.R.</a>; viewers derive pleasure from the sounds created by extra-loud crunching, slurping and lip smacking. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Craig Richard, 49, a professor of physiology at Shenandoah University and the creator of a website dedicated to the study of A.S.M.R., said that while the phenomenon is not medically diagnosed, people who enjoy A.S.M.R. experience a sensation of \"sparkling brain tingles\" while viewing \"trigger\" videos.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">On a recent Tuesday, Mrs. Gaskin sat down in her home studio for a recording session <!-- -->with her son Dalvin<!-- -->, who is 25 and something of a prot\\xe9g\\xe9, and his friend Nicole.<!-- --> On the walls were plaques commemorating the day she reached the one-million-subscriber mark on YouTube, as well as <!-- -->a framed letter from Susan Wojcicki, the C.E.O. of YouTube.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Mrs. Gaskin began the show with a friendly singsong greeting: \"What's up my Bloveleez?,\" a nickname she uses to refer to her viewers. Then she announced the night's meal, elongating the vowels in \"seafood boil\" as a soccer commentator would when announcing a goal. </p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Before diving into her food, she said a brief prayer: \"Heavenly Father, in the name of Jesus, I thank you for this food I'm about to receive. In Jesus's name, I pray. Amen.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-79elbk\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper\"><div class=\"css-z3e15g\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-wrapper-hidden\"></div><div class=\"css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15\" data-testid=\"photoviewer-children\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/fashion/11mukbang-filming/merlin_155878533_b6d5a11b-d730-4813-9455-07339ade3bbc-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Mrs. Gaskin's husband and manager, Nate Gaskin, adjusts a camera. Her YouTube career began with home-cooking tutorials.\\xa0\"Then I did a mukbang, and people just went crazy,\" she said.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Credit</span><span>Maddie McGarvey for The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">The food was strategically positioned on a <!-- -->serving tray<!-- -->, with the most colorful items on top and accented by bright yellow lemons and corn on the cob. On the table in front of the tray were three glass bowls of Mrs. Gaskin's homemade Smackalicious sauce. She wants to manufacture the spices used in the sauce so viewers can make their own.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">Before taking the first bite of food, Mrs. Gaskin, Dalvin and Nicole<!-- --> <!-- -->briefly paused in front of the camera. They posed with a crab leg, and, while smiling, they sang the word \"thumbnail.\" After the photo, the real action began. Once Mrs. Gaskin dipped her food into her Smackalicious sauce, she took her first bite and closed her eyes as she chewed.</p><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">While nodding, she said, \"Yup, umm hmm y'all, this is good.\"<strong class=\"css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10\"> </strong>She used slurping noises to indicate that something was juicy, followed by more head nods and \"yup\" utterances, as well as some vaguely orgasmic sounds. Dr. Richard said that these \"mouth sounds,\" in combination with Mrs. Gaskin's \"kind and positive disposition\" and the abundance of the food, are textbook A.S.M.R. triggers.</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn\"><div class=\"css-53u6y8\"><p class=\"css-exrw3m evys1bk0\">In Mrs. Gaskin's house, these kinds of table manners aren't punished but celebrated. She and her Bloveleez slurp and chew noisily and, as she put it, \"unapologetically.\"</p></div><aside class=\"css-o6xoe7\"></aside></div><div class=\"css-a7yk8a e73j0it0\"><figure aria-label=\"media\" class=\"css-kyszhr e1g7ppur0\" itemid=\"https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/06/11/fashion/11mukbang-cooking-2/merlin_155877846_af8f8dc9-7a77-4bbd-894b-c5b3a5e05ea6-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp\" itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" role=\"group\"><div class=\"css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0\">Image</span><div class=\"css-zjzyr8\"><div data-testid=\"lazyimage-container\" style=\"height:257.77777777777777px\"></div></div></div><figcaption class=\"css-1l6g02d e1xdpqjp0\" itemprop=\"caption description\"><span class=\"css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0\">Mrs. Gaskin prepares food to eat on camera.</span><span class=\"css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90\" itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\"><span class=\"css-1ly73wi
